Furthermore, the aircraft carrier "Ark Royal," etc., have all arrived outside the port, preparing to surround and attack the German warship (United Press, 16th).

Capital of Uruguay: According to unconfirmed sources from the National Socialist Party, Germany is concentrating warships and submarines along the coast of South America to meet the "Admiral Graf Spee" when it leaves the port of Montevideo and engage in battle with British warships (United Press, 16th).

Uruguay Lodges Strong Protest to Britain and Germany; Accuses Them of Violating the "Panama Declaration"; Uruguayan and Argentine Navies Implement Joint Patrols

New York: According to a Montevideo dispatch published in "The New York Times," Uruguay has taken measures to send strong notes to Britain and Germany regarding the Anglo-German naval battle, with an attached sea chart indicating that part of the battle occurred within the mouth of the River Plate, and warships from both sides at one point fired at each other within the three-mile limit. The note further points out that this battle took place within the 300-mile neutral zone around the Americas recently stipulated by the Pan-American Conference. Although the River Plate is more than 300 miles wide, the governments of Argentina and Uruguay both believe that once it enters the river, it falls under their jurisdiction. Therefore, the engagement of British and German warships therein has violated international law. The Uruguayan government has announced that the navies of that country and Argentina have established a joint patrol to prevent the recurrence of such naval battles (Reuters, 16th).

London: Reuters has learned that London officialdom has not received actual dispatches regarding Uruguay's protest due to the naval battle between the British cruiser and the German pocket battleship "Graf Spee" (Reuters, 16th).

Washington: Secretary of State Hull announced yesterday that the 21 American nations may convene a meeting to discuss countermeasures regarding the Anglo-German battle in the American "security zone" off the coast of Uruguay. If this meeting does take place, it will be convened in Panama. At the Pan-American Conference held in Panama in mid-September, it was resolved that Panama would be the intermediary between the American countries and the belligerent nations (United Press, 16th).

British Official Boasts of Naval Battle Victory

London: Secretary of the Navy Churchill telegraphed the New Zealand Minister of Defence to express his appreciation for the meritorious service of the crew of the British cruiser "Achilles," of which more than 300 members were from New Zealand. According to naval officials, in the battle in the South Atlantic, four members of the "Achilles" were killed and three were wounded. The casualty numbers of the other two cruisers, "Exeter" and "Ajax," will also be announced as soon as possible. The German pocket battleship "Graf Spee," which fought against the three British cruisers, was equipped with six 11-inch caliber guns, firing shells weighing 670 pounds. It first engaged the "Ajax," which only had 6-inch caliber guns firing 100-pound shells. The German warship then exchanged fire with the "Achilles," but the "Achilles" had the same firepower as the "Ajax." Finally, the "Exeter" rushed forward to engage, but the "Exeter" had slightly stronger firepower, equipped with 8-inch caliber guns that could fire 256-pound shells. Moreover, the "Graf Spee's" broadside weighed a total of 4,708 pounds, while the British cruisers' combined broadside weighed only 3,126 pounds (Reuters, 16th).

German Soldiers Who Died in Action Given Funeral; British Merchant Fleet Presents Wreaths

Capital of Uruguay: Thirty-six officers and soldiers of the German pocket battleship "Admiral Graf Spee" who died in action in a naval battle with three British cruisers were given a funeral here recently. Officials from the German legation, the Italian minister, and many officers from the Uruguayan army and navy attended to offer condolences. There were a total of 21 wreaths, one of which was inscribed with "To the brave warriors of the naval battle, from the British merchant fleet" (Havas, 15th).

Soviet Government Considers Breaking Off Relations with Britain and France; Germany Hopes for Early Peace Between Soviet Union and Finland; Netherlands Explains Reason for Abstention

Paris: The *Journal des Débats* reports from Sweden that after the League of Nations announced , the Soviet government is now considering breaking off diplomatic relations with and . However, Premier Voroshilov does not seem to mind, and German Ambassador to the Soviet Union Schulenburg also seems indifferent, contrary to general expectations. German leader Hitler, on the other hand, seeks to intimidate Sweden. Although the Swedish government recently proposed negotiations with Germany, was rejected and received a German note with a warning nature. This is likely the reason why the country's representative to the League of Nations dared not take a positive attitude (Havas, 16th).

Berlin: Regarding the League of Nations' expulsion of the Soviet Union, German political figures believe that it will not lead to any changes in the current situation, nor will it provide any benefit to Finland, as what Finland hopes for is clearly more effective assistance. Germany believes that Finland should negotiate peace with the Soviet Union as soon as possible and should not intensify its attitude. As for Chamberlain's claim that Germany seeks to exploit the Soviet-Finnish conflict to threaten the Scandinavian countries, German political figures denounce it as malicious slander, not worth refuting. German newspapers have been commenting on the League of Nations' activities, all saying that the League has only two powerful countries, which is not significant (Haitong, 16th).

Amsterdam: A Dutch semi-official figure issued a statement last night explaining the reasons why the Netherlands voted in favor of expelling the Soviet Union from the League of Nations, pointing out that the League of Nations Secretary-General launched a movement to aid Finland, convening League member states to jointly help the attacked country. The Netherlands considered whether supporting this appeal meant willingly participating in the Western European warring factions or whether it was a collective action of League members. As a result, it was decided before the vote to state that the cooperation of the Netherlands did not mean participating in collective action of the League, but rather contributing its technical assistance to Finland based on humanitarian principles. The Dutch semi-official figure continued, stating that the Dutch government believes that the League of Nations in its current state does not have sufficient power to implement international actions to sanction aggressor countries. This expulsion of the Soviet Union is actually because the Soviet Union first distanced itself from the League (Haitong, 16th).

Paris: After the League of Nations announced the Soviet Union's expulsion, it was generally expected that the country would launch a fierce counterattack. Diplomatic figures here also stated recently that although the Soviet Union has not yet broken off diplomatic relations with the countries that voted in favor of this move in the League of Nations General Assembly and the Administrative Council, one cannot immediately assume that this matter is over just because the country has remained silent so far. To what extent the country's aggressive attitude may develop in the future will depend on its strength and its interests. As it stands, the actions of the Scandinavian Peninsula countries are most noteworthy. Because Germany is currently touting the good relations between Germany and the Soviet Union, it is carrying out activities in the Scandinavian Peninsula countries, namely, on the one hand, acknowledging that these countries are under threat from the Soviet Union, and offering to intercede with the Soviet Union for these countries, and on the other hand, making it a condition that these countries accept the neutral policy it dictates (Havas, 15th).

Soviet Authorities Comment on League of Nations Resolution; Believe It Stems from a Conspiracy by Britain and France; Lacks Political and Moral Force

Moscow: Regarding the League of Nations Administrative Council's decision on the 14th to "expel" the Soviet Union from the League of Nations, Soviet authorities have issued a commentary. TASS is hereby authorized to announce the following:

The League of Nations Administrative Council's decision on December 14th to "expel" the Soviet Union from the League of Nations and to condemn "the Soviet Union's hostile actions against Finland" is, in the Soviet Union's opinion, only enough to provoke ridicule and make its unfortunate creators a laughingstock. First of all, we must solemnly point out that this resolution of the Administrative Council was passed under the direction of the ruling classes of Britain and France, and they have absolutely no moral or formal right to talk about "the issue of aggression." Britain and France have long seized vast territories in Asia and Africa, and still act arrogantly, controlling everything. Recently, they also rejected Germany's peace proposal aimed at ending the war early, and insisted on continuing the war until "ultimate victory" is achieved. These two facts alone are enough to expose the aggressive policy of the British and French ruling classes, making them less inclined to talk about the definition of aggression, and aware that they have already abandoned their moral and formal right to criticize others' "aggression," especially their qualification to comment on whether the Soviet Union is "aggressive."

Secondly, we must point out that the relationship between the Soviet Union and Finland has been defined by the Treaty of Mutual Assistance and Friendship concluded on December 2nd between the Soviet government and the People's Government of the Democratic Republic of Finland. This convention fully guarantees the peaceful relations between the Soviet Union and Finland, resolves the issue of safeguarding Finland's independence and the security of Leningrad, as well as the Soviet Union's transfer of its territory to Finland, so that the Karelian region can return to its homeland in a manner satisfactory to both parties. According to this convention, the Soviet Union exchanged an area of 70,000 square kilometers with a population of over 100,000 for Finland's territory of less than 4,000 square kilometers with a population of approximately 25,000. If the main definition of aggression is the seizure of another country's territory and the forced control of the people of the occupied area, then the world seems unable to deny that the convention concluded between the Soviet Union and the Republic of Finland is not only not an act of aggression, but rather a practical demonstration of the Soviet Union's peaceful and friendly policy towards Finland, aimed at safeguarding Finland's independence and expanding its territory to make it stronger. Conversely, if the current Britain and France were to encounter such circumstances, there is no doubt that their actions would be completely different. They would brazenly invade Finnish territory, as they did in the past when they invaded India, Annam, Morocco, and Soviet territory in 1918-1919.

Finally, we must point out that the Treaty of Mutual Assistance and Friendship between the Soviet Union and the Republic of Finland is confirmed to fully guarantee peace between the two countries. It is precisely for this reason that the Soviet Union not only does not wage war on Finland, but also has no intention of doing so. Those who, under the direction of a third country, violate the will of the Finnish people and cause Finland to wage war on the Soviet Union are none other than the now bankrupt Mannerheimite old Finnish rulers who do not want this convention to be realized.

Therefore, the real purpose of the League of Nations Administrative Council's resolution is not to strive for peace or to aid the Finnish people, but rather to aid the bankrupt Mannerheimite reactionaries who oppose the Finnish people, thereby further igniting the flames of war by forcing the Finnish people to be dragged into a war caused by Mannerheimite provocations. If the League of Nations were still a "tool for peace," its current mission should be to strive to end the war between the British-French bloc and Germany. However, the current member states of the League of Nations are not doing this, but are declaring their support for the policy of the Mannerheim-Tanner challenge faction in Finland, taking the path of inciting another war in northeastern Europe. Therefore, the League of Nations, under the manipulation of its current directors, has been transformed from a possible "tool for peace" into a genuine tool for the British-French military bloc to continue and incite war in Europe. Judging from this obscure transformation of the League of Nations, its resolution to "expel" the Soviet Union is not surprising. Since the imperialist gentlemen have decided to turn the League of Nations into a tool for safeguarding their war interests, they must find an excuse to expel the Soviet Union, because the Soviet Union is the only force capable of opposing their imperialist conspiracies and exposing their aggressive policies.

The League of Nations and its already discredited prestige willingly do this, we have nothing to say. However, if we investigate thoroughly, those who benefit from this may ultimately still be the Soviet Union. First, the Soviet Union will no longer bear the moral responsibility for all the League of Nations' ignominious actions. All responsibility for "allowing the Soviet Union to remain outside the League of Nations" will be borne by the League of Nations and its British and French directors. Second, the Soviet Union is no longer bound by the League of Nations and can be completely free.

The process by which the League of Nations prepared and passed the aforementioned anti-Soviet resolution is itself sufficient to reveal the conspiracy by Britain and France to achieve the aforementioned purpose. Everyone knows that there are a total of 15 countries on the League of Nations Administrative Council, and only 7 countries voted in favor of "expelling" the Soviet Union this time, which is a minority. The other 8 countries either abstained from voting or did not attend. These 7 countries that voted in favor of "expelling" the Soviet Union are Britain, France, Belgium, Bolivia, Egypt, the Union of South Africa, and the Dominican Republic. Thus, the "representatives" of Britain and France, with a combined population of only 89 million, plus the 5 countries of Belgium, Bolivia, Egypt, the Union of South Africa, and the Dominican Republic, with a combined population of only 38 million, decided to "expel" the Soviet Union, with a population of 182 million. What's more, in order to obtain this number of votes, the British and French representatives even had to change the composition of the League of Nations Administrative Council on the eve of the vote by special conspiratorial means, namely, by passing the League of Nations General Assembly, recommending the representatives of the Union of South Africa and Bolivia (the latter having been re-elected) as non-permanent directors of the Administrative Council, and the Egyptian representative as a so-called temporary director. Therefore, among the 7 directors on the Administrative Council who supported "expelling" the Soviet Union, 3 were temporarily and specially elected.

The fact that British and French representatives conducted this kind of conspiracy within the League of Nations has definitively eliminated any political and moral force of the results of the vote on December 14th. It is undoubtedly due to the fact that the League of Nations is entirely controlled by an atmosphere of political reaction and moral corruption that this kind of conspiracy can occur. What value can there be in a resolution of the League of Nations passed in this kind of atmosphere (TASS, 16th)?

Italian Mount Vesuvius Volcano Erupts

Naples, Italy: Mount Vesuvius, which has recently been heavily covered in snow, has suddenly erupted again. This morning, a torrent of boiling lava over 650 feet wide flowed out, and it is feared that the crater will be exposed again, which will cause immense disaster. The authorities are now preparing to evacuate the residents of the villages near the volcano (Reuters, 16th).

Western Front Warfare Gradually Intensifies; British Prime Minister Inspects Expeditionary Force

Paris: Although the warfare on the Western Front is still limited to encounters between patrol teams and reconnaissance teams, it has gradually intensified, and the number of soldiers on both sides in the encounters is increasing day by day, and the fighting is becoming more fierce. In the past 24 hours, two strong German reconnaissance teams approached the British lines on the Lys River, and their activities almost reached the level of an attack. In the Vosges area, where the border line passes through the forest, about 30 to 40 French and German soldiers engaged in a fierce battle that lasted for quite a long time (Reuters, 16th).

London: British Prime Minister Chamberlain began his tour of inspection of the British army in France yesterday, and has arrived by plane at an airfield behind the British lines, accompanied by Major General Ismay, Secretary of the British Imperial Defence Committee. The British Prime Minister and others were traveling in ordinary planes, which were protected by several fighter planes. After arriving, Chamberlain had lunch with Viscount Gort, Commander-in-Chief of the British Forces, and then drove to the Air Force Headquarters to inspect the battle charts and various arrangements. The British also saw the work in the telephone switchboard room in the underground room, where there were 1,400 telephone calls every day, and as many as 200 in each hour. The war correspondents at the Air Force Headquarters were all received and talked to by the British Prime Minister. One reporter said, "It is difficult to write about the war." An officer interjected, "Worry is better than bombs." The British Prime Minister said, "From my point of view, this is a matter of personal preference, but as far as I am concerned, I would rather worry than be bombed." The French people welcomed the British Prime Minister's tour of France very much, which was indeed a characteristic of the British Prime Minister's trip (Reuters, 16th).

Berlin: According to an announcement made here today, from the 18th of this month, from 8 PM every night to 7 AM the next morning, all borders with Denmark, the Netherlands, Belgium, Luxembourg, and Switzerland will be closed, and only regular trains will be allowed to pass through. It is heard that this measure is to prevent the illegal entry of spies (United Press, 16th).

Brussels: Gunfire was heard booming at sea off the coast of Belgium today, and the nature seems quite serious (Reuters, 16th).

President of Panama Dies

Panama City: Dr. Arosemena, President of the Republic of Panama, passed away yesterday at the home of his brother in Boquete at the age of 61. The cause was heart disease. The doctor still had nine and a half months left in his presidential term. The doctor had been in politics for 30 years, during which time he held important public offices such as Supreme Court Justice, Governor of Colón Province, Minister of Agriculture and Public Works, Minister of Interior, and Minister of Foreign Affairs, and also served as a representative to the League of Nations and the Pan-American Conference. The doctor was also an experienced journalist and served as the editor-in-chief of the Panama Daily for a long time (United Press, 16th).

Philippine Draftee Training

Manila: According to news from here today, another 20,000 draftees will graduate from the 13 training centers in the Philippines in the middle of next week. These people have received five and a half months of military training. Since this national defense system was established in 1937, there have been six classes of draftees trained, with 20,000 people in each class. According to this plan, by the time the Philippines becomes independent in 1946, there will be 400,000 people, and by 1966 there will be 1.2 million people (United Press, 16th).

The Chinese Army Counterattacks Chao'an City; Fierce Battles Along the Chao-Shan Railway

A Shantou dispatch states that on the morning of November 12th, just as the sky began to brighten, twelve Chinese Air Force planes suddenly appeared over Chao'an City. They divided into four groups to control the airspace and circled over the Japanese positions for approximately forty-five minutes. Amidst the anti-aircraft fire network of the Japanese forces on Hulu Mountain, they dove down to drop bombs, moving back and forth with ease. Zhugao Mountain, Jinshan, the West Lake Station, the East Gate Warehouse, the Japanese barracks at the Han Wen Gong Ancestral Hall on Hanshan Mountain, and the Japanese artillery positions were all hit and caught fire, destroying military supplies, vehicles, and more. The Japanese suffered over a hundred casualties and significant losses. On the 15th, three more planes appeared over Dahao, dropping over ten bombs on the Japanese warships docked there. The Japanese warships scattered in panic, and it is rumored that they also suffered considerable losses. The large army from Anjie Luhua launched a two-pronged attack on Chao'an City on November 13th, engaging in bloody battles in the northern and southern suburbs. The plainclothes special forces of the Chinese security forces attacked everywhere in Fuyang, Anbu, Chengcheng, Dongjin, and Yunbu, killing thirty to forty Japanese soldiers in each location. On the morning of the 14th, the Japanese army moved out from Caitang in several directions, creating disturbances. Over forty Japanese soldiers carrying machine guns fiercely attacked Hailian Mountain, engaging in a standoff for an hour before the Japanese forces collapsed and retreated. On the morning of the 15th, over five hundred Japanese soldiers from Caitang, supported by seven mortars and covered by three planes, advanced north along the railway line towards Wuyang Mountain and Zhanglin Bridge. Japanese aircraft dropped forty to fifty bombs on the Chinese positions, causing the Chinese army to retreat over ten *li*. That evening at 9:00 PM, Chinese reinforcements arrived and retook Zhanglin Bridge. Also on the morning of the 15th, the Japanese army's Nozoe unit, entrenched in Chao'an City, joined forces with puppet troops in an attempt to break through the Chinese encirclement. They concentrated their firepower on West Lake Mountain, supported by four heavy cannons and over a hundred artillerymen, first bombarding the Tongqiao Shimuwei area, and then advancing on the Chinese positions on Aoding Mountain, using artillery to cover the infantry's advance. From morning till night, fierce battles continued. They charged down the mountain several times, but were annihilated by the Chinese army, leaving behind over a hundred corpses. By the 16th, the Japanese offensive had been thwarted, and they had completely collapsed. The Chinese army regained the upper hand and controlled Chao'an City.

Shaoguan, Guangdong Province: Strict Prohibition of Japanese Goods; Qujiang County Takes the Lead

A Shaoguan dispatch states that the Qujiang County government, in order to strictly prohibit the promotion and sale of Japanese goods, has specifically formulated temporary measures for long-term prohibition and inspection of Japanese goods, as follows: (1) In order to first eliminate Japanese goods in Shaoguan City and eradicate their source, the government has specially organized an inspection team, jointly organized by the government's investigation and prohibition group and local agencies and organizations, which will send personnel to participate. (2) Taking Shaoguan City as the starting point, eight inspection teams will be organized and divided into eight sections, each team being responsible for a section. (3) Each team will consist of three people, two of whom will be appointed by the government, and the remaining one will be invited to participate from local agencies and legal entities. In addition, the government will send one supervisor for every two teams, who will be responsible for overall coordination. (4) The inspection of Japanese goods, trademarks, and types will be clearly instructed in advance by the head of the government's investigation and prohibition group, who will work with the police to carry out the task in the designated section. (5) The identification of various categories of Japanese goods will temporarily use the "Compilation of Japanese Goods Trademarks" issued by the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Economic Affairs this year as the standard, supplemented by other modified trademarks. (6) After inspecting Japanese goods, the investigation and prohibition group will issue a receipt, which will be signed and stamped by the inspectors and given to the owner of the goods for safekeeping. If necessary, the owner of the Japanese goods may be required to provide a written guarantee to be available for questioning at any time, or they may be detained. (7) If there are still doubts about the seized Japanese goods, they will be sent to the appraisal committee for appraisal. If it is determined that they are definitely not Japanese goods, they will be returned to the owner. (8) The method of disposing of seized Japanese goods will be submitted to the government for approval on a case-by-case basis. (9) A letter will be sent to the Guangdong Provincial Anti-Smuggling Bureau, Renru Tax Bureau, and the county's tax collection office, etc., asking them to pay special attention to imported goods. If they are Japanese goods, regardless of whether taxes have been paid or not, they should be detained first in accordance with the telegram order and sent to the government's investigation and prohibition group for appraisal. If suspected Japanese goods are encountered, the same procedure must be followed in order to eradicate the source. (10) These measures will be implemented from the date of promulgation and will be submitted to superiors for record.

Rice Prices Also Expensive in Fujian Province; Due to Manipulation by Unscrupulous Merchants and Embargoes in Various Regions; Provincial Government Has Ordered Strict Prevention in All Counties

A Fuzhou dispatch states that the autumn harvest in the coastal and inland areas of Fujian Province this year has been very abundant, but rice prices have instead been rising daily. Currently, the price of rice in the coastal areas has risen from 15 yuan to around 30 yuan per *shi* in less than a month. The price of rice in the inland areas has also risen from 5 or 6 yuan to 12 or 13 yuan per *shi*, making it very difficult for the people to afford food. Large cities such as Fuzhou, Nanping, Quanzhou, and Xinghua have merchants and gentry jointly organizing price controls, but each *dou* still costs 1.7 or 8 yuan, causing the prices of other daily necessities to also rise accordingly. The biggest reasons for this are: (1) Merchants mistakenly believe that the transportation and sale of grain will be managed by the province, limited to only one grain department of a trading company, and many dare not raise funds for procurement and transportation. (2) A few unscrupulous merchants are unwilling to transport the rice they have obtained permits from the government to transport to the local area for sale, storing it midway to wait for higher prices. Large households in the countryside also hoard the grain they have collected, refusing to sell it. (3) People in various regions mutually prohibit exports, not only are they not allowed to transport to other counties, but this district is not allowed to transport to that district, and even this village is not allowed to transport to that village, resulting in this village having a lot of surplus rice, while the neighboring village has nowhere to buy rice. The above three reasons have led to the current situation of expensive grain and rice shortage in Fujian Province. The Provincial Assembly and the Provincial New Life Movement Association have both submitted relief proposals to the provincial government. The Provincial Assembly's proposals are: (1) Allow merchants to freely procure and sell. (2) Temporarily suspend the collection of rice taxes in various regions. (3) Provide as much convenience as possible to grain transport ships and do not completely block them. (4) Fair prices should be sought in various regions, they should not be too high, nor should they be too low. (5) Stipulate measures to crack down on hoarding and speculation. (6) Telegraph Jiangxi Province to allow this province to purchase rice. The Provincial New Life Movement Association's proposals are: (1) All transportation agencies in the province should give priority to the task of transporting rice. (2) Trading companies in various regions should fully mobilize to procure grain for relief. (3) Permits to procure rice should be issued quickly to all formal merchants. (4) Order all counties not to prohibit the export of rice and strictly prohibit hoarding and speculation. (5) Prohibit all unnecessary consumption, such as brewing wine, raising ducks, and making rice cakes. (6) Promote the movement to eat two meals a day and eat mixed grains. The relief measures that the provincial government has separately implemented are: (1) Strictly clarify rumors that the government only allows trading companies to transport and sell rice, and does not allow rice merchants to operate or hire ships to transport rice, causing rice merchants to take the opportunity to hoard and speculate, citing business closures, resulting in high rice prices. (2) Order all counties that grain within the province should be freely traded. Regardless of military or civilian agencies, if merchants hold permits to procure and transport rice or apply for permits to transport rice out, they should inspect and release them and should not obstruct them. (3) Offer rewards for reporting large households hoarding and unscrupulous merchants monopolizing. Once verified, in addition to severe punishment, the stored rice will be sold, and 40% of the proceeds will be offered as a reward. (4) Stop price controls from today and order rice merchants to freely transport and sell rice, gradually restoring the rice market, and explain to the people that price controls are not a fundamental solution to the rice shortage. (5) The trading company, transportation company, and provincial bank, three provincial-run business agencies, jointly plan to allocate funds to purchase rice and transport it to various regions for relief. Chen Xuan, the general manager of the trading company, went to Jiangxi yesterday to negotiate the purchase of a large amount of rice to be transported to Fujian. After these separate relief measures are taken, the price of rice in Fujian Province can be expected to fall.

Education Department of the Refugee Association Changed to Education Section

Since the second half of this year, the Shanghai Refugee Relief Association has seen an endless rise in the market prices of grain and various daily necessities, resulting in huge expenses for the association. Moreover, donations from all sectors of the refugee community have been decreasing daily, making refugee relief efforts even more difficult. In order to save money, all departments have been merged into one office since this month, reducing staff and tightening expenses. The reorganization has now been completed. The association is determined to continue promoting the education of refugee children as before. All of the original Education Department has been reduced in scope and renamed the Education Section. Various craft training classes formerly run by the Education Department have been transferred to a newly established Industrial Training Section, which will run training classes in various fields such as chauffeur, sewing, grass weaving, barber, wireless repair, nursing, Chinese and English typewriter, etc., and will continue to operate. However, the efficiency of the training must be increased compared to before. New industrial training plans are currently being drafted to improve training work, so that refugees can have good skills to support themselves.

Sichuan Provincial Government Decides to Significantly Increase Business Schools

(Chengdu, 15th) At the Sichuan Provincial Government meeting on the 15th, there were many resolutions on education. The important ones are: (1) The College of Education of Chongqing University will receive an additional 10,000 yuan in funding this year. (2) A business school will be allowed to be established at Chongqing University. (3) The Yibin County Junior Ordinary Agricultural Vocational School with Agricultural Course will be changed to the Provincial Yibin Senior Agricultural Vocational School. (4) The Western Border Cultural Institute will be changed to the Provincial Western Border Cultural Education Hall from the 29th year. (5) The equipment of various departments of the Provincial Chengdu Senior Industrial Vocational School was burned, and 20,000 yuan was allocated for repairs.

More Confidence in Winning the First Division Championship; Lido Defeated Portugal Yesterday; Achieving a Great Record of Six Wins in Six Games with a Score of Four to One; West Force and East Hanlai Both Suffered Defeats

Lido's hope for the Western Union Football First Division Championship is growing stronger and more confident. Yesterday at Yiyuan, they defeated Portugal 4-1, achieving a great record of six wins in six games. In the first half, Lido took a 2-0 lead. In the two games at the Racecourse, East Hanlai lost to St. Francis 2-4, and West Force lost to French Commerce 1-3. Since these British giants have each lost one and drawn one, there is no question about Lido's championship. Yesterday at Yiyuan, there were about 1,000 spectators. Portuguese veterans Ma Shan'er and Cora Sha played, but they were old and past their prime, not as good as before. Lido missed countless opportunities, otherwise, the score would have been much higher.

Lido: Lu Zhongen, Li Yichen, Zhang Lingen, Yan Shixin, Meng Yiliang, Jiang Zhaoxiang, Cao Qiuting, Sun Jinshun, Huang Kehou, Xu Wenkui, Wu Qixiang

Portugal: Su Ruo, Ma Shan'er, Aquino, Ma Han, Oliveira, Xue Erfo, Larson L. Luochai Liao, J. Luochai Liao Cora Sha, H. Lemidi

Lido Scored Two Goals First: Lido attacked first. Ma Shan'er was still powerful and defused the danger several times. Kehou got an assist from Jinshun and shot from 15 yards, but it was blocked by Ma Shan'er. After Wenkui missed a sure goal from outside the penalty area, he received a hook from Qiuting and lost another sure goal in front of the goal. It wasn't until 20 minutes that Marder lost his footing. Jinshun stole the ball and passed it to Wenkui. Wenkui kicked from seven yards and opened the scoring. Ten minutes later, Qixiang passed to Qiuting, who pressed down and shot, but Su Ruo pushed it out not far. Jinshun swept it in from five yards, making it 2-0. Not long after, Lido's Zhang Lingen was injured and left the field, playing with ten men. However, the attack did not weaken. At the end of the first half, Lido took a 2-0 lead.

High-Pitched Triumphant Songs: The second half started, and Lido was still playing with ten men. Zhaoxiang and Shixin served as defenders, Yichen served as center, Qixiang retreated to midfield, and Kehou temporarily filled the right wing. The Portuguese team was eager to win and attacked with seven men, but still showed no improvement. After ten minutes, Lido had a corner kick opportunity. Qiuting took it and it was well placed. Wenkui jumped up and scored again, making it 3-0. Two minutes later, the Portuguese team's five forwards advanced together. Cora Sha shot high from the crowd and the ball went into the net, pulling back a goal. After 20 minutes, Zhang Lingen returned to the field, and the five forwards resumed their original positions at the start of the game, greatly increasing their momentum. In just six minutes, Qiuting got the ball and dribbled forward, shooting high from the left corner. The ball was headed into the goal by Su Ruo, making it 4-1. The victory was secured. After that, Lido continued to attack quickly, but all shots went wide. Yiliang was injured and rested. Not long after entering the field, the referee blew the whistle, and Lido won 4-1.

Rice Market to Implement Price Limits Set by the Municipal Council Today; The Highest Price for Domestic Rice is Set at 40 Yuan per Shi; The Highest Price for Ke Xian Rice is Set at 33 Yuan; Prices Decrease Progressively for Medium and Lower Grades; Foreign Rice is Not Subject to This Rule

The rice-grabbing frenzy has spread to the central district of Shanghai, causing concerns about public order. He Dehui, the Chinese Affairs Officer of the Public Concession's Municipal Council, summoned Chen Ziyi, Zhu Zixiang, Zhou Zhizhen, Gu Yisheng, Lu Wenshao, Zhang Nianxuan, and other leaders of the city's rice industry to the bureau again at 10:00 a.m. yesterday to discuss the recent serious rice and grain problems. Three measures were jointly decided: (1) Resetting price limits: (A) The price of domestic rice must not exceed 40 yuan per shi, with prices decreasing progressively for medium and lower grades. (B) The highest price for Ke Xian rice must not exceed 33 yuan per shi, with prices decreasing progressively for medium and lower grades. (C) The prices of foreign rice are not subject to this rule due to fluctuating source costs. (2) Protecting the business of legitimate rice merchants: (A) He Dehui, the Chinese Affairs Officer of the Municipal Council, will immediately notify all police stations to increase protection and immediately notify the Director-General of the French Concession's Municipal Council by telephone to coordinate. (B) To avoid accidental losses, the plan to transport rice during curfew hours cannot be implemented because it conflicts with the office hours of the warehouses.

The Guild Resolved to Lower Price Limits

The Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Guild held its 58th joint meeting of directors and supervisors at 4:00 p.m. yesterday, attended by Xing Zhigang, Chen Ziyi, Fu Qiangeng, Cao Xinggeng, Zhu Zixiang, Yan Xiaoquan, Jin Zhaoyun, Huang Zhihe, Zhu Xiangsheng, She Bingwen, Cai Shengming, Gu Yisheng, Zhang Lizhong, Jiang Hongbin, and Hu Wen'an, a representative of the rice market. Chairman Xing Zhigang reported on the cases to be discussed and gave a brief explanation of the recent rice market situation. Two important cases concerning the rice market were then passed as follows: (1) Discussing the case of further lowering the price limits for rice and grain: It was resolved to comply with the Municipal Council's intention that, starting from the 17th of this month, the highest price limit for domestic white rice must not exceed 40 yuan per shi, with prices decreasing progressively for medium and lower grades. The highest price limit for Ke Xian rice must not exceed 33 yuan per shi, with prices decreasing progressively for medium and lower grades. The prices of foreign rice are not subject to this rule due to fluctuating source costs, so that it can still be imported continuously to alleviate the food shortage when domestic rice is blocked.

Calling on Authorities to Protect Rice Merchants

(II) Proposed letter to the authorities in the concessions requesting protection for legitimate rice merchants, resolved: Since the authorities in the concessions issued a proclamation stating that they would not protect hoarding merchants, there has been considerable misunderstanding in the outside world, leading to repeated disputes. Rice stores have experienced dozens of incidents of rice looting. Rice firms face dangers when selling goods, especially during delivery. Even sales of over a hundred bags, such as those by Dingxin Tai, have been suspected of hoarding. In such circumstances, all legitimate rice merchants are in danger. This affects not only the business of fellow traders but also the food supply of the entire city. It is necessary to write to the authorities in the concessions, requesting a detailed explanation of the meaning of hoarding for compliance. The association originally strongly supports public reporting, but we request a preliminary investigation and prudent handling. If there is indeed hoarding or manipulation, it should be severely punished; otherwise, it will easily lead to malicious accusations, harming the reputation of legitimate merchants, blurring right and wrong, and preventing effective protection to ensure business operations and maintain the food supply. It is also proposed to formulate and announce a notice on price limits, to be announced in the market today, for universal knowledge and strict compliance.

Rice Store Association's Emergency Meeting

The Shanghai Rice Store Trade Association held a temporary emergency executive and supervisory committee meeting at its clubhouse on Shanhai Guan Road yesterday at 3:00 PM. All committee members attended, with Lu Wenshao as chairman. The chairman first reported on the situation of the rice market and the results of his visit to the authorities. Then, various committee members offered their opinions separately. Subsequently, it was decided to appoint Zhang Nianxuan, Lu Wenshao, and Qu Zhenhua as three committee members to visit the police authorities in both concessions again, to strongly protect legitimate rice merchants, to maintain the entire rice market. It was also decided to continue the meeting this afternoon to discuss important cases. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM. The three representatives immediately went to the police stations in both concessions to report everything and request effective protection to maintain the business of legitimate rice merchants.

Regulation Association to be Established Tomorrow

After the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and over thirty other organizations resolved to establish the Shanghai Civil Food Regulation Association, they nominated Yu Qiaqing and ten others as committee members to actively prepare. They also convened a preparatory committee meeting yesterday at noon, attended by Yu Qiaqing, Xu Jilun, Xi Yushu, Li Wenjie, Wang Yuqing, Gui Yanfang, Zhang Jiguang, etc. At the meeting, Li Wenjie and others were appointed to draft the charter and rules of procedure. It was resolved to appoint committee members to discuss with the banking industry about advancing funds and to find ways to raise funds in order to purchase foreign rice and carry out price stabilization. The association is scheduled to be established tomorrow.

Abnormal Market Trading Stalled

Yesterday's tea party market for the rice industry at Qinglian Pavilion on Fuzhou Road saw almost no transactions after the market opened at 9:00 AM. The market closed early at 11:00 AM, effectively halting operations. It is said that this was due to the recent rice looting incidents and the measures taken by the authorities in both concessions to register hoarders and punish unscrupulous merchants. Sellers were eager to sell off their goods as soon as possible, resulting in a glut of goods, while stores were afraid of accidents after purchasing, so they were unwilling to buy, resulting in no transactions. However, this matter has attracted the attention of the general public. Some people believe that this action by the rice market is an excuse. The reasons for this are highly unpredictable, because the proclamation of the concession authorities clearly states that those who engage in speculation and manipulation will be punished, while legitimate rice merchants are fully protected, and concrete measures have already been taken. Moreover, the authorities are curbing rice looting, and all sectors are actively planning to regulate the food supply and seek fundamental solutions. The market situation may be difficult, but it should not be stopped due to minor setbacks, leading to a halt in market transactions and increasing public panic. It is hoped that the rice industry will quickly come up with a solution.

Movement for Integrity Most Encouraging for the Financial Sector

The integrity movement initiated by various sectors in the city has been expanding its publicity and actively promoting it in recent days, sparing no effort. It has deeply imprinted the concept of integrity in people's hearts, awakening them and achieving significant results. Yesterday was the fifth day of the publicity week, targeting the education sector. A letter to colleagues in the education sector was published, encouraging teachers to promote integrity, lead by example, guide young people, and promote the national spirit. Today is the sixth day of the movement, targeting the financial sector in Shanghai. While there are many far-sighted and conscious people in the financial sector, there are also many who only seek immediate gains and disregard the overall situation. They often use their large amounts of capital without thinking about investing in the interior to assist the country's economic construction, only knowing how to hoard in the isolated island, speculate and hoard, and monopolize prices, which is truly wrong. It is not only shameful to the nation but also betrays countless compatriots who are struggling hard. It is decided today to dedicate the exhortation to the financial sector in the city. In addition to distributing declarations and leaflets of the integrity movement, a letter urging the financial sector will be published, several thousand words long.

News of British Warship Victory British Expatriates Excited Officers and Men of the Three Ships Involved Have Close Ties with Shanghai

The Zi Lin News reported that the British cruisers Exeter, Ajax, and Achilles fought the German pocket battleship Spee for two days and won, and took measures to prevent the Spee, now sheltering in Montevideo Harbor, from re-entering the sea. British expatriates in Shanghai expressed their admiration for the heroic fighting of the three British cruisers upon hearing the news yesterday. Moreover, the three ships and their officers and men who participated in the battle have close ties with Shanghai. Harwood, who commanded the three British cruisers, is the commander of the British American and West Indies Fleet. He is well-known in the British China Fleet and served as the commander and executive officer of the British warship Cumberland from 1928 to 1929. At that time, the commander of the ship was Colonel Snape (later promoted to Rear Admiral). Another coincidence is that after Harwood ordered the attack on the German warship Spee, he has now met his old friend Cumberland. Several British warships, including Cumberland, have sailed to Montevideo to reinforce the British fleet to wait for the Spee to sail out. Commander Harwood is very famous on the Chinese coast and is a torpedo expert.

National Goods Company Employees Receive Pay Raise Subsidies Implemented Labor Dispute Resolved

Over eight hundred male and female employees of the three branches of the China National Goods Company on Nanjing Road went on strike to demand improved treatment from the management. The three branches were temporarily closed for two days. After continued negotiations between labor and management, and mediation by the Industrial Section of the Public Works Department, a satisfactory resolution was reached. The three branches resumed business at 9:00 AM yesterday. According to inquiries by reporters from the New Sound News Agency, the company's employee salaries are paid in two installments on the 15th and 30th of each month. The salary payment date for the first half of this month was delayed until yesterday due to the unresolved labor dispute. However, the employees' request for a pay increase of two yuan per person per month from January onwards was approved. As for employee subsidies, they will continue to be handled in accordance with the method determined by the management. Those with monthly salaries of two to five yuan will receive an additional two yuan if they live in company dormitories and three yuan if they live outside. Those with monthly salaries of six to nine yuan will receive an additional three or four yuan. Those with monthly salaries of ten to nineteen yuan will receive an additional four or five yuan. Those with monthly salaries of twenty to twenty-nine yuan will receive an additional five or six yuan. Those with monthly salaries of thirty to forty-nine yuan will receive an additional six or seven yuan. Those with monthly salaries of fifty to one hundred yuan will receive an additional seven or eight yuan. This will be implemented from this month.

Prospects for Factories in the Eastern District Cause for Concern Discontent Among Workers is Growing

The Continental News reported that yesterday (the 15th), it was heard that discontent among workers in factories in the Eastern District is growing, and the "workers' organizations" controlled by the Japanese are increasingly active among the laborers in the Eastern District. Regarding these "workers' organizations," further details were learned yesterday. The organization is located at 127 Yangguang Road and is officially named the "China Workers' Welfare Association." The official leader is a Chinese man surnamed Mo (transliteration) who is controlled by a Korean or Taiwanese man named Lang Qizhong (transliteration). Above Lang is Kubota, a retired colonel of the Japanese Army, who controls everything.

Cotton Yarn Detained on Manley Wheel Association Requests Inspection

The British merchant ship Shirley Wheel sailed to Wenzhou without approval, importing goods without authorization, violating regulations. The Wenzhou military authorities imposed a penalty of 30% on the goods on board. It is now heard that the cotton yarn transported to Wenzhou by two yarn companies, Zhu Guiji and Sui Feng, members of the Shanghai Yarn Industry Association, has also been penalized. Iron Gate at Xin Kaihe Continued to Open Yesterday Notice that the Walkway Has Been Changed to South Side Entrance and Exit No Sign of Other Iron Gates Opening

The iron gate connecting Xin Kaihe to the South City has been on trial opening since the 11th. After six days of smooth passage, it will continue to be opened. There is no sign of opening the iron gates at Lao Bei Men and other places, as it is still under consideration. The details are as follows:

Iron Gate Closed, Walkway Changed

Since the iron gate connecting Xin Kaihe to the South City began its trial opening on the 11th, over 20,000 residents have passed through. As the passage has been relatively smooth, it will continue to be opened from yesterday. However, the small doors on both sides of the previously opened iron gate have been causing crowding and difficulty in maintaining order. Therefore, the passage location has been changed to the channel on the south side of the fire brigade, in front of the door. The iron gate on the north side has been completely closed.

Implementation of Inspection, Good Order

The new passage on the south side is also equipped with wire mesh and divided into import and export lanes. Residents entering and exiting are still crowded. In terms of order, French Concession detectives and female inspectors are selectively inspecting suspicious individuals, with good results and no disturbances. Therefore, the French Municipal Council has decided to continue opening the gate to facilitate residents' entry and exit.

Other Iron Gates Not Opened

There is no sign of opening the other iron gates connected to the South City in the French Concession, as they are still under consideration. It is said that the Xin Kaihe gate alone is sufficient for passage, and the French Concession authorities have no intention of opening other iron gates for the time being. According to reporters from the Datong News Agency who inspected the iron gates at Xin Bei Men, Lao Bei Men, Nanyang Bridge, and other areas yesterday, in addition to the usual closure, the iron gates were densely covered with wire mesh, and armed police, detectives, and French soldiers were stationed there. The situation was extremely quiet.

Rice Looting Spreads

Rice looting has intensified in recent days. Initially, it was prevalent only in the Shanghai West area, but yesterday it spread to the concessions. The situation is as follows: (Public Concession) Rice stores at No. 100 Kaifeng Road, No. 15 Chengdu Road, No. 66 and No. 191 Dagu Road, No. 33 and No. 340 Shanhai Guan Road, No. 389 Baker Road, various Dazhonghua rice stores, and locations on Robert Road, Carter Road, Guanchang Road, and Jiaozhou Road all experienced rice looting incidents. (French Concession) The Dingtai rice store at No. 1111 Pushi Road suffered the greatest loss, with over a hundred sentences of white rice looted. Other rice stores, such as Yilong rice store at the intersection of Lafeyette Road and Caishi Road, Gongda rice store at the intersection of Albert Road and Fuxu Road, a certain rice store at No. 387 Jujida Road, and a certain rice store on Ganshi Dong Road, as well as Chang on Pingjihe Road and Dajiang on Ladu Road, were all robbed of varying amounts of white rice. A total of eighteen rice looting incidents were reported yesterday, with approximately eight hundred piculs looted. The accurate number of rice looting incidents that occurred the day before yesterday (the 15th) was thirty-six, with sixty-two people detained and a total of one thousand three hundred dan robbed. Statistics show that a total of fifty-four incidents occurred over two days, with two thousand one hundred dan looted and one hundred twelve people arrested.

Selling at Discounted Prices

Yifeng Rice Store, next door to Huayuanli on Bailinan Road, had over ten poor people attempting to break into the rice store yesterday morning. A certain employee, Mr. Jia, was very alert and said to the owner, "This store has a total of twenty-eight piculs of rice. Why not sell it at a low price to help the poor?" The owner agreed and sold it to the poor at twenty-eight yuan per picul (both indica rice and national rice were priced the same). In the blink of an eye, it was sold out. When the general public heard of this low market price, they flocked to various stores in Shanghai West to buy, but to no avail. As a result, the general public was extremely angry and almost resorted to rice looting again. The owners of various rice stores in Shanghai West, in view of this, convened a meeting at Hengyi Public Rice Store, No. 1105 Jisi Fei Er Road, at 1:00 PM yesterday. Over forty representatives attended to discuss effective ways to suppress rice prices. They unanimously agreed to standardize market prices, with the highest price for foreign rice not exceeding thirty-six yuan and the highest price for national rice not exceeding thirty-eight yuan. Those who violate the resolution will be severely punished. Huang Zhihe was appointed as the representative to report and file the resolution with the Shanghai Rice and Vegetable Trade Association and the Market Management Committee.

Police on Alert

After the rice looting occurred, all rice stores, large and small, in the French Concession closed, leaving only a small hole for small-scale transactions by ordinary people. The French Concession Police Department immediately ordered all police stations to order detectives to remain stationed in the police stations after the shift and not to leave without authorization, in case of an emergency to suppress the riots. It also ordered all patrol teams and armored vehicles to step up patrols to maintain order. Patrols on foot and in vehicles inspected each rice store in the concession every fifteen minutes to prevent rice looting from happening again.

The Continental News reported that Bowen, the Superintendent of the Public Concession Police Department, criticized the rice looting situation in the city last night (the 15th), saying that these disturbances may have been initiated by hooligans. The rice looting riots only occurred several days after the highest rice price of forty-eight yuan per dan had passed, and there were no riots when the rice price was at its highest. Robson, the Assistant Superintendent of the Police Department responsible for handling the rice situation, stated that the number of rice looting riots is not expected to increase significantly, and the Police Department is quite capable of handling the current situation. From today (the 16th), police officers in both concessions will adopt special patrol alerts in the rice store areas. In the Public Concession, almost all Chinese detectives will be stationed in the rice stores, while in the French Concession, patrol officers with light machine guns will patrol each rice store at regular intervals. Rice stores in both concessions will close at 5:00 PM every day.

Rice Merchant Assassinated

Shen Shangwen, a local resident, 63 years old, residing in the Weihe Sauce Garden at No. 145 Zhejiang Road, is engaged in the rice business and is one of the six major rice dealers in the city. He established the Yuande Rice Store at No. 145. Yesterday morning at around 10:00 AM, Shen took his private chartered car to go out, intending to go to the Qinglian Pavilion rice industry market at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Hubei Road to conduct his daily buying and selling transactions. Unexpectedly, when the car reached a small vegetable market on Fuzhou Road, two assassins suddenly jumped out from the roadside, stopped Shen's car, and one of them took out a pistol and shot at Shen, firing two shots in a row. One bullet hit Shen's left shoulder and went through his back, and the other bullet hit his foot. He immediately fell into the car. Seeing that their purpose had been achieved, the two assassins quickly fled. By the time nearby police officers heard the alarm and arrived, they had already disappeared. Shen Shangwen was taken to Renji Hospital for treatment, where doctors performed surgery. The injuries were not critical, and there was probably no major problem. The police station is strictly pursuing the perpetrators. However, after the incident, the general speculators in the Qinglian Pavilion rice market felt extremely uneasy.

Workers at Ewo and Xiang Mao Resume Work Yesterday

The labor strike at the Ewo Cold Storage at No. 5555 Yangshupu Road and the Xiang Mao Soap Factory at No. 2310 Yangshupu Road has been resolved. Workers at both factories resumed work yesterday morning. However, workers at the Ewo Brewery at No. 350 Dinghai Road and the Swiss Shanghua Aluminum Steel Refining Factory at No. 610 Meizhou Road are still on strike.

Ms. Mao Liying's Remains to be Encoffined Today Yesterday, Various Circles Went to Pay Their Respects to Her Remains He Xiangning and Others Sent Representatives to Shanghai to Offer Condolences

Ms. Mao Liying, Chairman of the Chinese Professional Women's Club, was suddenly attacked by two thugs near Sichuan Road on Nanjing Road at 7:00 PM on the 12th of this month, suffering serious injuries. She eventually died of ineffective treatment at 2:12 PM the day before yesterday. Friends and people from all walks of life believe that Ms. Mao devoted herself to social work during her lifetime and made great contributions to disaster relief. Therefore, the news of her death was extremely painful for all sectors. It is not only a loss to society but also a great loss to the country. Ms. Mao's friends and people from all walks of life have formed a funeral committee to handle everything.

Various Circles Sent Wreaths and Funeral Couplets

Ms. Mao's remains were examined by the coroner's office the night before last and sent to the Universal Funeral Home yesterday. Technicians at the funeral home performed makeup, and a public viewing was held at 2:00 PM yesterday. Over seven hundred people from all walks of life attended, and the funeral was extremely solemn. A large number of wreaths, couplets, and condolences were also sent. The couplets included "Exhausted Benevolence and Wisdom" from McLane High School and "Sacrificing Oneself for Righteousness" from Shanghai Women's Organizations. Those who sent wreaths included the YWCA, colleagues from the Jianghai Customs, Qixiu Girls' School, the Chinese Women's Mutual Aid Association, colleagues from the Shanghai professional community, the Shanghai All Circles Friendship Association, and individuals. Ms. He Xiangning specially sent representatives from Hong Kong to Shanghai to offer condolences and presented a condolence gift of one hundred yuan. Qian Xinzhi, Du Yuesheng, Huang Renzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Wu Shaowu, and others also sent representatives to Shanghai to offer condolences or sent couplets and condolence gifts by telegram.

Encoffined in Accordance with Religious Rituals

Ms. Mao's remains are scheduled to be encoffined at 2:30 PM today. Because Ms. Mao was a devout Christian during her lifetime, the encoffining will be held in accordance with Christian rituals, and a pastor will come to preside. It is heard that the procedure for the encoffining will begin with the pastor praying for Ms. Mao's remains, followed by a farewell ceremony from all circles. It is also heard that permanent memorial measures from all circles are being discussed. Ms. Mao's coffin will be temporarily placed in the Universal Funeral Home until the funeral at 1:00 PM on the 18th of this month, when she will be buried in the Hongqiao Municipal Council Cemetery.

Japanese Man Who Assaulted Police Sergeant Still Needs to be Summoned for Questioning

The three Japanese men (now known to include one Taiwanese) who assaulted a British police sergeant at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Zhejiang Road on the evening of the 13th were taken to the Japanese Consulate Police Station after being detained. They were released after being admonished by the Japanese Police Station. However, after their release, they still need to be summoned at any time. According to inquiries by reporters from the Dazhong News Agency yesterday, the Japanese Police Station has notified the police station authorities to provide written proof and requested the injured police sergeant, Mr. Jin, to accompany the British Army West Force Highlands soldier Stevens and the Public Works Department inspector McNeill, who rescued Mr. Jin at the scene, to testify at the Japanese Consulate Court after he recovers. They said that the two Japanese men and one Taiwanese man who caused the trouble would be prosecuted for assaulting public officials.

Yong An No. 3 Factory Labor-Management Dispute Resolved with Signature Yesterday Factory Accepts Mediation Method Union Representatives Consider Satisfactory

The strike dispute at Yong An Textile Factory No. 3, after mediation by Gu Bingyuan of the Industrial Section of the Public Works Department, and the advice for workers to resume work first and handle the dispute according to law, has been resolved with signature yesterday afternoon. The contract is recorded as follows: The labor-management dispute at this factory has been resolved as a result of mediation by Gu Bingyuan of the Industrial Section of the Public Works Department and various gentlemen from the Police Department. The factory has agreed to accept the following methods: (1) Ordinary workers who have served for more than one year will receive a year-end bonus of ten yuan per person. Workers who have served for less than one year will have their bonus calculated according to the number of months of service. (2) Wages will be paid as usual during the strike period. (3) The factory shall not dismiss workers without reason. The above methods have been deemed satisfactory and accepted by all worker representatives. Employer representatives Guo Qiong and Li Xizhao, worker representatives Yan Liujin and Wei Xuncheng, and eleven others, Gu Bingyuan of the Industrial Section of the Public Works Department, December 16, 1939.

Dredging Bureau Dredging No Definite Date Restoration After Two Years of Suspension Full of Twists and Turns

The English-language Great Beauty Evening News reported that the Japanese authorities had previously announced that the Dredging Bureau would resume work on December 1, and then announced that work would resume on January 1. This reporter asked customs officials this morning (the 16th) about the possibility of this. Their opinions were divided. According to a customs official, dredging work cannot begin until January 15 at the earliest because the Dredging Bureau's equipment has not been used for more than two years and therefore needs to be greatly refurbished. Another customs official said that since the Japanese authorities have agreed to assist in restoring dredging, work should be able to begin by the end of this year. Li Jiannan, the "Jianghai Customs Supervisor" appointed by the Nanjing government, refused to disclose any definite date for the Dredging Bureau to resume work, but said that he hoped to begin work "soon."

Two Chinese Detectives to be Released Tomorrow

Two Chinese detectives, Sun Peihe and Xu Jianbi, who were performing their duties at the intersection of Robert Road and Binglang Road in the Public Concession on the 19th of last month, were detained by the Japanese military police due to a conflict with a puppet official. The Concession authorities were quite concerned about this matter. Later, the Japanese side transferred the two Chinese detectives to the pseudo "Shanghai West Court." Yesterday afternoon at around 2:00 PM, the pseudo court interrogated them without authorization. The pseudo official who caused the incident and the Japanese military police were all present. Eventually, it was "announced that the two Chinese detectives were not guilty" because they were performing their duties in accordance with the law and there was nothing wrong with them. However, since today is a Sunday, they are scheduled to be released tomorrow.

Chen Xianzhang Kidnapped

Chen Xianzhang, from Yuyao, Zhejiang, 34 years old, once served in a social organization. Last night at around 9:00 PM, an old friend suddenly invited him to the Shalivan Tea House on Nanjing Road. When Chen Ying responded to the invitation and walked to the front of Shalivan, he found that his old friend was already waiting there. Immediately, he and Chen boarded a car and sped northeast. Someone witnessed a total of three cars parked there at the time, with several strong men standing by, which seemed to be a planned action.

An Interesting Journey from Changsha to Ningbo

Dr. Geling, Acting Principal of Xiangya Pharmaceutical College in Changsha, recently arrived in Shanghai and described to a reporter from the North-China Daily News the details of his journey from Changsha to Ningbo. The trip covered 950 miles and was accomplished by car, boat, and rickshaw in just seven short days. The journey was filled with exciting and extraordinary events.

Traveling Down the Xiang River

Dr. Geling set off from Changsha at the end of October, heading south to Xiangtan. Because the roads in that area were damaged, he had to travel down the Xiang River. The main channels of the river had been carefully laid with mines by the Chinese army, but the dangerous locations were clearly marked with tall flagpoles extending above the water's surface. Vessels dispatched by the central government were stationed at the ends of the minefields to prevent boats from entering the dangerous zones.

In the Autumn Sunshine

On the second day of his journey, Dr. Geling continued in the warm autumn sunshine, sailing from Xiangtan to Lukou, passing through several scenic and mountainous rural areas. About an hour from Xiangtan, Dr. Geling came to the "graveyard" of boats, where he saw sailboats, sampans, and motorboats stranded on sandbars, most of them completely destroyed. These boats were apparently wrecked after drifting downstream and running aground.

From Lukou to Hengyang

After arriving at Lukou, Dr. Geling had his luggage unloaded and boarded a midnight train to Hengyang. There were still quite a few trains running on the railway. The one he took to Hengyang was a blue steel carriage formerly used on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway. Upon arriving in Hengyang, Dr. Geling joined Mr. Burke, and they traveled together by car. They bought a five-gallon can of gasoline for fifty yuan and arranged the back of the car for sleeping. They set off on a clear Saturday afternoon for Chaling, 126 miles away. They parked by the roadside at night to sleep and started driving again at dawn, arriving in Chaling, where they bought a well-cooked breakfast consisting of rice, eggs, peanuts, and tea for only thirty cents. After breakfast, they resumed driving.

From Hunan into Jiangxi

Upon crossing the border from Hunan into Jiangxi, there was a checkpoint, but Dr. Geling and his companion were quite surprised that their car wasn't even stopped. They drove straight into Jiangxi. There were several policemen stationed at the checkpoint, but they paid no attention to the travelers. The area was also a long-distance bus station because passengers had to change buses when traveling from one province to another. Long-distance buses from Hunan were not allowed to operate in Jiangxi, and vice versa.

Spending a Night in Xingguo

For the hundred miles east of the border, the road ran through a narrow valley, and the road surface was excellent, making travel easy. The roadside was quite desolate. Starting from Hengyang, they traveled for a day and arrived at the bustling small city of Ji'an around noon on Sunday. Although the city had been slightly bombed, it had recovered, and business was thriving. Dr. Geling and Burke bought a five-gallon can of gasoline in Ji'an for forty-five yuan. They set off from Ji'an and drove in the rain to the small town of Xingguo. As dusk fell, eight or nine young Chinese men with flashlights approached, holding cards for inns. Several of them spoke English fluently and claimed that the inn they represented was the best. Dr. Geling and Burke eventually looked around and chose a brand-new inn to stay in. They later learned that the innkeeper had previously run an inn in Nanchang and now established inns in various towns along the highway.

People in a Painting

After resting for a night in Xingguo, Dr. Geling and Mr. Burke continued on to Ningdu, traveling through newly opened roads in a mountainous rural area. Although the bright sunshine gradually dried the accumulated rainwater from the previous day, the road was still difficult to navigate, especially on the slopes. They drove along the road past steep cliffs made of black and white sandstone. Dr. Geling said that the captivating scenery of the area was unlike anything he had ever seen before.

Everywhere, There Were Coal Blocks

After a while, they drove past a granite mountain and witnessed a very astonishing sight. The road was opened through a large coal seam, and there were coal blocks even on the road surface. People carelessly threw this black mineral to the roadside. The engineers who built the road were too busy and had no time to pay attention to the coal blocks that were dug up when the new road was opened. Moreover, the area was quite backward, so coal blocks were not valued and were discarded by the roadside for several miles. This example vaguely reminded people of China's undeveloped rich mineral deposits.

After the quiet mountains, a towering and solitary mountain suddenly appeared. The mountain was a light color and stood tall into the clouds. The faint color was not due to snow but to some kind of substance flowing freely from the peak, covering one-third of the mountain. The mountain seemed to have been mined. The two travelers stopped and talked to a farmer who happened to be passing by. The farmer told them that the top of the mountain was made of limestone, and this type of stone had been mined for hundreds of years. The old roads on the hillside used hundreds of years ago were still clearly visible. In recent years, dynamite had been used to mine limestone. Workers used dynamite to blast, and the large stones rolled freely down the slope.

Car Almost Caused Disaster

Dr. Geling finally continued driving and arrived in Ningdu, stopping at the church. Ningdu itself was not affected by the war. Many sugar canes were planted in the suburbs. The two stayed at the church for a while and then drove north to Yingtan. When they arrived near the city at midnight and were about to drive over the railway bridge, the car slipped sideways, and one wheel slid off the bridge, almost causing an accident. Fortunately, they stopped in time. As the two were thinking about how to get the car back on the road, a group of Chinese arrived. They claimed to have taken refuge in the area from Nanchang, but they seemed to be well-nourished. Dr. Geling gave them a small reward, and they found wooden planks and managed to get the car back on the road.

Heard Air Raid Alert

The two drove on to Yingtan and left Yingtan the next day. They arrived in Shangrao for breakfast in the morning. Although the city was small, it was quite prosperous. The two found a restaurant and enjoyed a fine breakfast of ham and eggs. They also bought gasoline in Raozhou for thirty-five yuan per five gallons. As they were about to finish filling the gasoline, an air raid alert sounded. They jumped into the car and quickly drove out of the city to take temporary refuge. Looking back, they saw soldiers on the city walls also taking refuge in shelters for safety. Dr. Geling and others continued to drive along the highway and saw that the grains around the city were particularly abundant, and many rice paddies were planted nearby.

Xikou Reception Center

They then entered Zhejiang from Jiangxi and stopped in Jinhua. However, they heard another alert before entering the city and had to stay outside the city until dusk. They bought some gasoline again in the morning for twenty-five yuan per five gallons. They drove to the lovely small town of Xikou. The town was prosperous because it was an overnight stop on the journey. There were several large hotels in the town, one of which was operated by the China Travel Service. There were also China Travel Service reception centers in many places along the road, maintaining a standard of prescribed prices and facilities.

Never Saw a Single Soldier

The two handed over the car in Xikou to someone returning west and then set off for Ningbo. For the first three hours, they traveled by rickshaw and then changed to a boat to Ningbo, a distance of ten kilometers costing four yuan. But they soon discovered that traveling by the regular riverboat between Xikou and Ningbo cost only twenty cents and was faster. Dr. Geling arrived in Ningbo, completing his 950-mile journey. They never saw a single soldier along the way. Of course, the two avoided the war zones, but it was quite remarkable that such a vast area was never touched by the Japanese army. Dr. Geling plans to spend a short time in Shanghai and then return to Changsha by the same route.

Falsely Impersonating a Name to Intimidate and Defraud a Copper and Tin Shop Owner, Sending Two Letters and Threatening by Telephone, Detectives Design to Arrest Multiple Criminals Successively

Shen Rongchun, the owner of Shen Gui Ji Copper and Tin Shop at No. 816 Beijing Road, received a threatening letter delivered on the morning of the 3rd of this month. The letter was signed by the "General Headquarters of the Shanghai Youth Anti-Japanese Iron-Blood Punishing Traitors Group". Afterwards, the bandits repeatedly called Shen Gui Ji, and the shop assistants told them that the owner was not in Shanghai and that they could request a subsidy from the trade association. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 14th, another bandit delivered a letter to Shen Gui Ji. The bandit held an object that looked like a hand grenade. Upon inspection by the people in the shop, it was found that the letter continued the request of the previous letter, and the time was still in the French Park on the afternoon of the same day. However, Shen and others still ignored it. restaurant to discuss. So he took the Wu suspect to Juxing Garden and asked Wu to write a request for guests to summon his accomplices. threatening group was led by Wu Genfa, and Zhang Xuemei was responsible for delivering the second threatening letter. All Public Bathhouses in the City Jointly Raised Prices Again Yesterday, Changing Each Ladle to Fifteen Wen, Five Times Higher Than Before the War

Since the price of fuel coal has soared, restaurants, hotels, and eateries have all been greatly affected and have raised prices one after another. Yesterday, all hot water industries (i.e., public bathhouses) in the city also jointly announced a price increase of 50%, changing from ten wen per ladle to fifteen wen per ladle, and also announced, "The price of coal has skyrocketed and we will be forced to close down. We will temporarily increase prices, which has been decided by the industry to maintain our capital and relieve our immediate needs. We hope for the understanding of all sectors." (According to the industry, three ladles were sold for ten wen before the war, two ladles after the war, and one ladle was changed to one wen in October. In two years, the price has increased nearly five times, setting the highest record for price increases.) At the same time, tea houses have also raised prices by one or two cents each due to the coal price. Other small food and snack shops have either increased prices or reduced ingredients to compensate. The livelihoods of ordinary people are increasingly difficult.
