Commercial News

Grain, The Time When Foreign Rice Is in Demand, Rice Shops Are Involuntarily Closed

Only a Little Trading in Small Bazaars, No Goods Are Sold to Rice Markets, High-Quality White Japonica Rice Is Limited to 40 Yuan

Since the price of rice has soared, ordinary people (not just the poor) have difficulty getting food and are all in desperate need. Due to the rice rush that spread over the past two days, rice shops all closed their doors yesterday and stopped doing business. Some shops continued to trade as usual in small bazaars, which was a great inconvenience to the common people. Since the rice shops were effectively closed, they did not sell rice to the market, so the rice market was also effectively closed and closed at 10:30 a.m. without any transactions. It is said that the closure of the rice shops was to prevent robbery, but it also had side effects and was intended to restore the old state. This is related to the people's food and cannot be taken lightly.

Yesterday, 1,600 to 1,700 bags of foreign rice from Jiangxi, Beijing, and Anhui arrived. More goods are expected to arrive in Shanghai one after another. However, the merchants have stopped buying for a long time, and the shops are afraid to add goods after the rice rush. The sellers are very eager to sell, but there was no showing in the involuntary closure yesterday, so only a few hundred bags were traded all day. Jiangxi rice was opened at 33 yuan to 32 yuan, which was a small decrease of a few cents to nearly one yuan compared to before.

The orders for foreign rice are arriving in succession. There is no agreement on new transactions. Only a few hundred bags of spot goods were sold in the involuntary closure yesterday. Saigon was 33 to 34 yuan, and 31 yuan 8 jiao to 31 yuan and a half, which was a small decrease of a few jiao to one yuan compared to the previous day. There was no trading in transit goods.

Yesterday, another 9,000 bags of foreign rice were imported, which were transported by the Taikoo Company's Qiongzhou ship. Among them, 1,002 bags were loaded from Saigon and 8,138 bags were loaded from Hong Kong. The ship docked at the company's wharf in the French Concession for unloading. It is heard that the Suzhou and Nanning ships arriving in Shanghai next week will also transport large quantities of foreign rice. (Zu)

At 4:00 p.m. yesterday, the Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Association held its 58th joint meeting of directors and supervisors. It was decided to invite the intention of the Engineering Bureau that the maximum price of white japonica rice should not exceed 40 yuan in legal currency per stone, and the intermediate price should be reduced successively. The maximum price of foreign rice should not exceed 33 yuan in legal currency per stone, and the intermediate price should be reduced successively.

Dull Trade in Flour and Wheat

Flour Yesterday, the trade in spot flour was dull. Because it was the weekend, both local and foreign customers were digesting slowly. The Hakka helpers mostly adopted the same cage goods. It is heard that the price of Green Cannon carriages is still 9 yuan, and the rest are also 2 to 3 jiao higher than the factory price. Less than 30,000 bags were traded in the general market. Financial - The Exchange Market is Mediocre

Yesterday’s foreign exchange market saw no movement in HSBC’s listed rates. The informal British and American exchange market was quiet due to the weekend, with operators generally taking a wait-and-see attitude. The half-day situation remained calm, trending tight initially then receding, ultimately ending slightly firmer than the previous day. In the morning, the British-American exchange rate was reported to have shrunk, causing the opening to show a weak British pound and a stable US dollar. Subsequently, due to frequent settlements by foreign firms, and foreign banks such as HSBC seizing the opportunity to raise prices to cover demand, a slightly weaker state appeared. The British pound reached 4 shillings, 5 pence, 625 points, and the US dollar reached 7 yuan, 46 cents, 875 points. Soon, fewer buyers appeared, and because foreign banks, such as HSBC, Banque Belge pour l'Étranger, and a certain other bank, were still eager to supply, the situation reversed to become slightly firmer. At noon, under stabilized conditions, the market closed with the British pound at 4 shillings, 5 pence, 9375 points, and the US dollar at 7 yuan, 53 cents, 125 points, each weaker by 0.03125 compared to the previous day. As for futures trends, they were no different from the spot market. Midway through the day, there were rumors of December-January swap trading, with HSBC bidding 0.09375 US dollars against a certain Chinese bank, for a combined monthly interest rate (excluding commission) of slightly more than 1.2%, although arbitrageurs realistically only saw about 0.8% to 0.9%.

Gold Market Calm - Half-Day Trading Approximately One Thousand Yuan

Yesterday's cash raw gold unofficial market situation was such that because the exchange market was easing, coupled with the fact that the Hong Kong gold price, the only outlet, was not as robust as in the previous two days, and due to the weekend, general long positions weakened, and there was a strong desire to close out positions. As a result, the price fell by a small 19 yuan. However, the morning opening carried over the previous night's momentum, continuing to rise by 10 yuan, to a high price of 4,190 yuan. Shortly after, a certain money exchange business took advantage of the high price to aggressively sell, and the situation suddenly weakened, falling by 20 yuan. At that time, the foreign exchange market was slightly tight, and the market briefly stabilized, but soon the exchange market hardened, and securities firms quickly shifted to selling, and retail investors also followed suit to close out positions, falling to a low price of 4,160 yuan. Later, Hong Kong gold prices rose, but this failed to attract followers, and speculators had no effect. Therefore, the noon close was only 4,161 yuan. In the afternoon, the off-exchange market stabilized, with prices at 4,165 yuan to 4,170 yuan. Half-day trading totaled just over one thousand taels. Jewelry gold prices remained unchanged. Customs gold prices also remained flat.

Raw Gold Down 19 Yuan

Since the morning opening, each bar (ten taels) carried over the previous day's momentum, and securities firms still had purchasing interest, pushing up the market by 10 yuan. Seeing this situation, buyers stopped, and the price fell by 20 yuan. Cash shops sold 30 taels to money exchange businesses for 4,170 yuan. Subsequently, because the exchange market softened slightly, sentiment improved, and a certain gold shop, on behalf of speculators, took the lead in buying, rebounding by 15 yuan. Gold shops bought 10 taels from securities firms for 4,185 yuan. Then, because the foreign exchange market suddenly softened slightly, securities firms frequently released their holdings, and at that time, there were few buyers. The price fell again, dropping by 25 yuan. Gold shops sold 20 taels to money exchange businesses for 4,160 yuan. At that time, Hong Kong gold suddenly commissioned a certain gold shop to buy several hundred taels, immediately pulling the price up by 10 yuan. Money exchange businesses did 10 taels among themselves for 4,170 yuan. After that, buying interest subsided, and securities firms continued to sell, dropping back to a low price of 4,160 yuan. Money exchange businesses bought ten taels from securities firms for 4,163 yuan. Later, another money exchange business sold 50 taels to securities firms for 4,161 yuan as the noon closing price. Sunday Supplement Winter Special

A Page of Historical Material on the Yunnan Uprising - Cai Songpo Rising Up to Punish Yuan

— Gong Huai

The Yunnan Uprising was a continuation of the 1911 Revolution, a struggle against autocratic regimes. It wrote a glorious page in the history of the nation. Although the targets of these two revolutions were different, as the 1911 Revolution aimed to overthrow the corrupt Qing government and the Yunnan Uprising aimed to overthrow the traitorous Yuan Shikai government, their value and significance were equally great. When we commemorate this heroic revolutionary action, we cannot fail to pay our highest respects to the wise and courageous General Cai Songpo!

Yuan Shikai's Imperial Dream

Since Yuan Shikai seized the presidential throne with the strength of the Beiyang warlords and bureaucrats, he stepped up the implementation of policies to eliminate revolutionaries, hoping to change the state system and satisfy his imperial craving with the support of his henchmen. By 1915, Yuan's imperial conspiracy was fully exposed. Externally, he borrowed huge amounts of foreign debt without the approval of the Senate, which he used to raise troops and purchase weapons, preparing to deal with revolutionaries who opposed the monarchy. He did not hesitate to cede sovereign rights and humiliate the country, recognizing the independence of Tibet in exchange for the understanding of the United Kingdom, and signing the Twenty-One Demands as compensation for Japan's permission for him to become emperor. Internally, in addition to intensifying the massacre and imprisonment of revolutionaries, he instructed his henchmen to organize the so-called "筹安会 (Preparatory Society for Peace)," advocating a monarchy. At the same time, he secretly telegraphed his henchmen distributed in various provinces, ordering them to jointly telegraph to urge him to advance. After a hypocritical show of humility, on December 12, he openly ordered himself to be emperor, changing the era name to "洪憲 (Hongxian)." Thus, this monkey crowned himself and clumsily took the stage.

General Cai Enticed into Beijing

General Cai Songpo was originally a soldier with revolutionary ideas. After graduating from the Japanese Military Academy, he joined the army and participated in revolutionary work. After the founding of the Republic of China, he was promoted to governor of Yunnan for his military achievements. Yuan, with his deliberate plans to become emperor, naturally regarded such an iron-willed man with suspicion. Therefore, before his conspiracy was exposed, he ordered the removal of General Cai's military power. Still not feeling at ease, he transferred General Cai to Beijing, to serve as a director of the Sutra Compilation Bureau, a position with no real power. After entering Beijing, General Cai saw through Yuan's intentions. Because secret agents were always by his side, he was under Yuan's strict surveillance and was already like a tiger in a cage.

Clever Escape Through a Fake Banquet

Although General Cai was in a dangerous situation, he did not show any emotion on his face, mingling with the Yuan faction day and night, indulging in lavish entertainment, pretending to be in "this happy place, not thinking of Shu," causing Yuan's suspicion of him to gradually fade. To avoid implicating his wife, he secretly discussed a plan. General Cai deliberately indulged in pleasure outside, and Mrs. Cai deliberately quarreled and even fought with him. As a result, Mrs. Cai went to the judicial衙門 (Yamen) to complain, saying how outrageous and careless General Cai was about his family, requesting a divorce. General Cai also pointed out in court how shrewish his wife was and was willing to divorce. Seeing that both parties were willing, the judicial official granted the divorce. Mrs. Cai jumped out of the tiger's den and packed her bags to return to her hometown in Hunan. General Cai was secretly delighted that the initial plan had succeeded. One day, he held a large banquet somewhere, inviting many military men and bureaucrats. When the wine was half drunk, General Cai claimed to have something to do and excused himself, saying he would return in a while. Those of the Yuan faction and the secret agents sent by Yuan did not suspect anything because General Cai was the host today. General Cai then called a rickshaw to the station. Near the station, he bribed the rickshaw puller and exchanged clothes with him in a secluded place, mingling in the noisy crowd. He took a train to Tianjin. Then, he quietly boarded a Japanese ship to Japan, transited through Annam, and returned to Yunnan. On that day, by the time the Yuan faction realized it, General Cai had already boarded a Japanese ship and safely escaped.

The National Protection Army and the Demise of Hongxian

At this time, Tang Jiyao in Yunnan, although he had military power, hesitated to raise troops to punish Yuan, fearing that he was isolated and weak. Just as he was undecided, General Cai happened to escape back to Yunnan, so he strongly urged Tang Jiyao to raise troops to protect the country and oppose the monarchy. He himself served as the commander-in-chief of the First National Protection Army, and together with Li Liejun, commander-in-chief of the Second Army, fiercely attacked Sichuan and Guangdong, with irresistible force. At the same time, Liu Xianshi, governor of Guizhou, and Lu Rongting, governor of Guangxi, also rose up in response. Almost half of the southwest was filled with an atmosphere of punishing Yuan. When the news reached Beijing, Yuan realized that the situation was not good, and even his "confidants" had defected. Under feelings of worry and anger, on March 24, he had to order the abolition of the monarchy. The life of "Hongxian" was only 83 days, and the generation of traitor Yuan Shikai had a short imperial dream and soon departed from this world.

Christmas and Disaster Relief Movement —Hoping All of Shanghai Will Actively Promote It—

— Xing

This year's Christmas is the third celebration since the war. Although various sectors continue to hold celebrations every year, they are still much less joyous than before the war. However, if we calculate the consumption spent on celebrating Christmas, the amount must still be astonishing!

On Christmas Eve, the dance halls, bars, and cinemas all over Shanghai are filled with a different kind of festive scene; they have all turned into earthly paradises, indulging in extravagant pleasures, filled with joy and excitement, celebrating wildly. The consumption for one night can range from dozens to hundreds of yuan per person. At the same time, let us look back at the refugees this year, exposed on the streets, without clothes or food, in a terribly miserable situation. The other day, the weather suddenly turned bitterly cold, and in one day, more than fifty refugees and coolies in the two concessions were frozen to death. Others who barely survive are countless. What's more, in the current situation of extremely high living costs, the lives of the poor are even more severely oppressed. These many poor refugees are eagerly waiting for you, great philanthropists, to donate and provide relief, so I propose a Christmas disaster relief movement. Generously donate money to be used for refugee relief, which will definitely save many refugees. Then, celebrating Christmas will be more meaningful.

Furthermore, I hope that all dance halls, bars, and cinemas in Shanghai will hold fundraisings for winter clothing donations on that day. If some prizes can be added to reward the generous philanthropists and increase the interest of donors, the income from donations will definitely be exceptionally enthusiastic!

Finally, I also hope that people from all walks of life can naturally participate in this Christmas disaster relief movement, appealing for the refugees and creating blessings for them.

Various Aspects of Christmas

— Xinliang

Turkey

As soon as Christmas arrives, all the food stores on Avenue Joffre have already hung up beautiful and eye-catching turkeys. Europeans and Americans regard turkey as the only delicacy on Christmas Day, so there are countless people in Shanghai who have seen their preferences and are doing seasonal business. Speaking of turkeys, those produced in the United States are the best, fat and delicious, costing more than ten U.S. dollars each; Zhoushan, China, is also known for producing turkeys, but compared with American turkeys, Zhoushan turkeys are ultimately inferior, because they are inferior in terms of breeding and breeding methods compared to the American methods. Therefore, if we want to recover the outflow of rights and interests, we must go through extensive research and improvement.

Christmas Cake

According to Western customs, every time Christmas arrives, in addition to preparing turkey as food, the most popular thing is this kind of Christmas cake. Every housewife must make a large, white-capped cake on Christmas Eve for the whole family to celebrate Christmas. According to general people, eating this white-capped cake is not only delicious but can also bring unexpected good luck in the coming year.

Santa Claus

A face full of snow-white beard, wearing a red suit, carrying a full bag on his back, descending to the world in a reindeer sleigh—this person is our old friend we call "Santa Claus." Almost every child in Europe and America likes the arrival of this old friend, because from him, children can get countless toys. Although children know that this "Santa Claus" is just a character in people's imagination, because of the customary tradition, there are still "foolish children" who take off their socks to wait for him to send gifts. In the world full of gunpowder smoke, would "Santa Claus" be unhappy to come to the world again, dear children, have you ever thought about it?

Christmas Card

It is said that Christmas cards originated in England, but we don't need to worry about the date of its birth here. At present, every major city in the world has this kind of "Christmas card" popular, and it can be said that everyone likes it. The so-called "Christmas card" is originally a few thin sheets of paper with a few congratulatory words written on it, or a beautiful picture drawn on it, to be sent to relatives and friends to congratulate them on good luck in the coming year. At first, this habit of sending greeting cards only existed between Christians, until in the most recent century, this custom has spread to people of all classes around the world.

Christmas Tree

The Christmas tree is also a kind of decoration in Christmas. Children like to put all kinds of small candles or toys on the tree, and then hold hands around it, singing and dancing, to celebrate Christmas. These Christmas trees, some large and some small, are covered with red, green, gold, and silver streamers, and some are specially equipped with small electric lights, with various colors complementing each other, which is really extremely beautiful.

All in all, everything about Christmas symbolizes a peaceful, beautiful, and joyful scene; let us wait for the coming of bright and brilliant days.

Mourning Couplet for Cai E by Liang Rengong

— Wenyi

General Cai Songpo studied at the Hunan Ziqiang Academy in his early years, and Mr. Liang Rengong deeply valued his talent. Although Liang and Cai had different political views, their friendship as teacher and friend was very strong. After Yuan's defeat and death, General Cai also died of overwork. Rengong wrote a eulogy to express his grief and also wrote a mourning couplet saying:

"I saw the son go forth but did not see his return; Heaven has not yet abandoned this culture, yet how could it bear to abandon this worthy man?

Comparing the early death of the General to the death of Yan Hui, expressing the utmost grief and pity.

Proclamation at the Time of the Yunnan Uprising

The Republic has been established for four years.

Various countries recognize it, and there is internal and external peace.

The Head of State violates the law and betrays his oath.

He establishes an imperial system and changes things arbitrarily.

The Five Nations warn of impending doom.

The Military Government hereby declares the great righteousness.

Sincerely advises the abolition of the imperial system.

Restore our Republic and expand the people's spirit.

All these actions are taken out of necessity.

They are only directed at the Central Government.

The province is safe, and all order is maintained as usual.

All citizens, do not be alarmed.

Students, do not believe the rumors.

This proclamation is hereby issued for the knowledge of all.

Unofficial History of the War of Resistance, Part 1: Christmas in Wuhan, 1937. 33. Madame Chiang Kai-shek Asks Chairman Chiang to Eat Turkey. The Price of a Turkey is Twenty-Five Yuan.

Another Christmas season is here. Let me tell you a Christmas story during the War of Resistance.

According to Western customs, a turkey must be served in the dishes to celebrate every Christmas holiday. In the winter of 1937, when Chairman Chiang commanded the army and was stationed in Wuhan, he was really very hard. On the eve of Christmas, Madam Soong Mei-ling felt that even though she was busy with military affairs, Chairman Chiang was working so hard for the country and should be happy on this festive season. She immediately called Huang Renlin, the director of the New Life Movement General Association, and told him her intention, and ordered him to buy a turkey immediately. Huang Renlin obeyed the order and ordered the secretary Wei Chunzeng to do it. Wei Chunzeng immediately took a car to various chicken shops to buy turkeys. Unexpectedly, in such a big Wuhan, he could not buy a turkey. Wei Chunzeng was quick-witted. He thought that if he could not buy it in the city, why not look for it in the countryside? He immediately drove the car out of the city. It was really a coincidence. Soon after the car left the city, he found a turkey next to a farmer's thatched house. Wei Chunzeng was overjoyed when he saw it, and immediately jumped out of the car, ran into the thatched house, and asked the farmer to buy the turkey. It happened that things are often not as expected. The farmer said that the turkey was for breeding, and he would not sell it no matter how much it cost. This made Wei Chunzeng at a loss. He thought about it and had to tell the reason, telling him that the chicken was bought for Chairman Chiang to eat. This moved the farmer's heart, and he finally sold it for twenty-five yuan. When Chairman Chiang and his wife had dinner together on the first day to celebrate the festival, there was a turkey dish on the menu.

Page 16

Talking About the Winter Solstice Festival

— Li Binglu

Explanation of the Winter Solstice

The Winter Solstice is also known as the Longest Day. The Book of Rites says, "In the middle of winter, the days are shortest," so it is also called the Shortest Day. The Dream Record says, "The capital attaches the greatest importance to the Winter Solstice Festival, changing clothes and offering sacrifices to ancestors, just like the New Year." According to the Book of Song, Ritual Records, "During the Wei and Jin dynasties, the Winter Solstice was the day when all countries and officials congratulated the emperor, so a small meeting was held, which was second only to the New Year's Day," so the Winter Solstice is also called the Sub-Year. But what is the Winter Solstice? According to the Interpretation of Calendrical Meaning, "The sun travels in the sky to the southeast corner of Xun Wei and reaches its extreme here, so it is called the Winter Solstice." As for the "arrival" (至) in the Winter Solstice, it also has a origin. Let's look at what the Classic of Filial Piety says: "The Big Dipper points to Zi for the Winter Solstice, and arrival has three meanings: first, the arrival of the extreme of Yin; second, the arrival of the beginning of Yang energy; and third, the sun travels to the south, so it is called arrival."

Anecdotes of the Winter Solstice

There are also many anecdotes about the Winter Solstice Festival. During the Jin and Wei dynasties, the palace used red threads to measure the shadow of the sun, and after the Winter Solstice, the length of the day increased by one thread. In the Tang dynasty, the palace used women to measure the length of the day, and after the Winter Solstice, the day increased by the work of one thread compared to normal days. Therefore, Du Fu's Winter Solstice poem says: "Every day, worry follows the lengthening thread." In ancient times, every time the Winter Solstice came, the market was closed for three days, and people hung curtains and gambled, which was called "Celebrating the Festival." According to the Book of Changes, Tonggua Yan, "During the Winter Solstice, the ruler brings in the eight talents, or tunes the Yellow Bell, or tunes the Six Laws, or tunes the Five Elements, or tunes the Law Calendar." Linghu Chu's Table states that building Zi is the origin of the Three Subtle Things, and the Yellow Bell is the foundation of the Six Laws. When the winter air arrives, the Wall Star is in the middle." According to the Ming Dynasty's Comprehensive Canon, every Winter Solstice Festival, the emperor bestows mink fur hats on the officials, and the emperor wears new mink fur. During the Winter Solstice Festival in the Han Dynasty, people wore crimson robes. The Ritual Records of the Later Han Dynasty says, "During the Winter Solstice, all officials in the capital wear crimson." During the Kaiyuan period of the Tang Dynasty, there was heavy snow, and the eaves dripped into icicles. A concubine asked a servant to knock off two branches to look at and play with. The emperor asked what they were, and the concubine laughed and said, "These are ice tendons." During the Jin Dynasty, there was a man named Zhou Yi, whose courtesy name was Boren, whose mother was Li, whose courtesy name was Luoxiu, who gave birth to Yi and Songmo, who were all in prominent positions. During the Winter Solstice, she raised a cup and gave it to her three sons, saying: "You are all noble, what else do I have to worry about?" Song said, "I'm afraid it's not as good as your will. Yi has great ambitions but short talents, which is not the way to preserve oneself. Song is straightforward and not tolerated in the world. Only Anu is mediocre and always in my mother's sight."

Nine-Nine Elimination of Cold

Binzhou's Five-Cover Mountain determines the price of rice based on the amount of snowfall during the Winter Solstice each year. Therefore, the Unified Records says, "When the Five Covers are covered with snow, rice is as cheap as dirt." Cao Zhi's Memorial says, "I have seen in the old rituals that the country offers shoes and socks during the Winter Solstice to welcome fortune and step on longevity." In recent ancient times, women often offered shoes and socks to their mothers-in-law on the Winter Solstice to step on the meaning of longevity. In ancient times, during the Winter Solstice, people painted a branch of plain plum blossoms with eighty-one petals, dyed one petal each day, and when all the petals were dyed, the Nine-Nine was over, and spring was deep, which was called "Nine-Nine Elimination of Cold Picture."

The Day Before the Winter Solstice

Du Shi's note says, "The day before the Winter Solstice is the Lesser Solstice." But according to the Tang Dynasty's General Records, "The Lesser Solstice is the second day." The Old Study House's Notes says, "(The day before the Winter Solstice is called the Winter Stay, which is opposite to the New Year's Eve, which is the Min dialect)." Lu Zhi's Biography says, "That night is the Winter Solstice New Year's Eve." From this, we can know that the Tang people also called the day before the Winter Solstice the New Year's Eve, so there is the sentence "The sun and the moon are removed" in the Poetry of Tang Style.

Winter Solstice Customs

According to legend, Gonggong had an incompetent son who died during the Winter Solstice and became a plague ghost who was afraid of red beans, so during the Winter Solstice, people cooked red bean porridge to ward off evil. Jiao's Classification of Forests says, "During the Winter Solstice, at midnight, comb your hair one thousand two hundred times to praise the Yang energy, and at the end of the year, the five organs will circulate, which is called the immortal hair washing method." In Luoyang, people fry Green Pearl every Winter Solstice and wear a Yang scarf on their heads. In Wu's customs, people attach great importance to the Winter Solstice Festival, saying that it is a fat festival and a thin year, and they give each other festival gifts. Liu Shilang Du Yin has a poem that says, "Every family talks about etiquette during the festival, and it takes a lot of effort to welcome and send."

Random Talks on the Winter Solstice in Various Places

— Fuyun

Although the people in various parts of our country have different customs for the annual Winter Solstice Festival, they all attach importance to this day. Now, I will write down the Winter Solstice activities that I have personally experienced and publish them in this journal. I think the readers will also want to hear about them.

People in Ningbo attach more importance to the Winter Solstice Festival than to Qingming; those who work away from home mostly return to their hometown to worship their ancestors before the Winter Solstice, which has been passed down for many years and is highly valued. Although it is the same as the Qingming Festival, they worship their ancestors at home (Ningbo calls it making soup rice, and the character "soup" is pronounced like the syllable "gang"). The ancestral halls in the countryside perform operas. Because Qingming is exactly when the farm work begins, the Winter Solstice is when the year's crops have been harvested, and there are more people available. If the year is a good harvest, they are particularly extravagant in their performances for the ancestral halls, and they do not hesitate to spend more money. In addition to worshiping their ancestors, there is also a "security" act of respecting gods, which is said to be a wish for peace and security in the home during the year (Ningbo calls it the twenty-ninth night), which is different from other places.

The act is performed within three days before and after the Winter Solstice Festival, or on the Winter Solstice itself. They use yellow paper and ink brush (a piece of yellow paper one foot long and four inches wide) to write the two big characters "保安" (Security) on it, and then write two lines below, one line for the month of this month (that is, the day of respecting the gods) and the line below for the surname of the family who is doing the offering. The time for respecting the gods is uncertain in the morning and afternoon, but most of them are in the afternoon. They use a pair of yellow candles, or green candles, but most of them use green candles, and insert green incense in the middle. They offer chicken, fish, and meat as three animals, fruits, three cups of clean tea, and the number of wine glasses is determined by the number of months in the year. For twelve months, they use eleven glasses, and for the intercalary month, they use thirteen glasses. A basin of burning charcoal is placed in front of the table, and another basin of clear water is placed next to the basin to take the meaning of peace between water and fire. They also make a kind of rice flour cake, which is four inches in diameter, mixed with sugar in the flour, solid without filling, with sesame seeds on it, called Winter Solstice Cake.

People in Shanghai's rural areas also attach great importance to the Winter Solstice. For example, if a family has a new bereavement that has lasted for three years, there is an act of "taking away the spirit tablet," which means "removing the mourning" or "taking off the mourning" (in various parts of northern Jiangsu, after three years of mourning, it is called taking off the mourning). They are usually held on Qingming or Winter Solstice. That is, on the morning of the Winter Solstice, they first invite the spirit tablet on the spirit platform to the ancestral hall, and then put all the elegiac couplets, as well as all the hanging plain objects, and the table for offering the main item, into the river together, taking the meaning of throwing away the bad luck. When removing the spirit table, the movements are very agile, called "taking away the spirit platform," and the Taoist priest recites it once before removing it. Shanghai's customs also regard the Winter Solstice as a ghost festival, and there is also a local folk song: Winter Solstice night (pronounced as "ye" sound), put out at every house, if you have it, eat all night, if you don't have it, cry all night. Although it is a superstition, it is also to persuade future generations not to forget their roots and to be careful in pursuing their ancestors.

Casual Talk about Christmas

— Shi Wenda

If you are often out and about, then you will definitely see that the major companies, dance halls, churches, and other places are decorated exceptionally brilliantly and pleasing to the eye. This is the Christmas of Europeans and Americans. Because this day is often two days after our country's Winter Solstice Festival, some people give it an elegant name and call it "Foreign Winter Solstice."

Historically speaking, Jesus was not born in the year 1 AD, but in 4 BC, which was about the time of Emperor Ai of the Former Han Dynasty in our country. He was born in Bethlehem Village in the country of Judea. Let us examine whether his birthday is on December 25th.

According to the biography of the new four gospels, "When Jesus was born, shepherds came to worship. However, although Palestine is located in the eastern Mediterranean, its climate is continental, so the winters are very cold. Shepherds could not possibly be in the fields doing pastoral work. From this, we can know that December 25th is not a correct day. Then the reader will ask, why did later generations choose this day as Jesus' birthday?

We must know that in ancient Greece, the Greeks regarded the birthday of the Egyptian sun god RE as a carnival. Later, the Romans also inherited this festival. Therefore, in the early fourth century, a Pope in Rome changed the birthday of the sun god to celebrate the birth of Jesus.

In the middle of the fourth century, Bishop St. Nicholas of Myra used money to help poor children on Christmas Day. Later, it was adopted by various places and became the origin of today's Santa Claus giving gifts to children.

Winter Solstice: The Rebirth of Yang – The Astronomical Winter Solstice

— Guan

The Winter Solstice of each year invariably falls on the 21st, 22nd, or 23rd of December in the Gregorian calendar. However, there's no fixed date in the Lunar calendar, so you have to consult an almanac. The Summer Solstice, Spring Equinox, and Autumn Equinox are similar. For example, the Spring Equinox is in the third month after the Winter Solstice, which is the 20th of March in the Gregorian calendar next year. Originally, these four solar terms divide the year into equal parts, each getting a quarter. The attached diagram shows the situation of the Northern Hemisphere on the Winter Solstice, with short days and long nights, and the arrow indicates the sunlight coming in.

As the sun revolves in its orbit, on the day of the Winter Solstice, its light shines directly on 23.5 degrees south of the equator, which is Australia, the South African Federation, Paraguay, etc. After that, it gradually moves towards the northern part of the Earth, crossing the equator and reaching 23.5 degrees north of the equator, which is the Summer Solstice. This year's sunlight, its time. Because the sunlight moves, the person has a Yang Sheng thought is: draw a gradually longer. According to the truth, the two times the direct sunlight crosses the equator, that is, the Spring and Autumn passed the Winter Solstice the Earth's northern part in our country's ancient "Winter Solstice a language, meaning over the Winter Solstice and night gradually shorter air should also gradually hot, but the Earth's heat has been over a long period of emission, must be repeated storage, coupled with the northern cold wind invasion, the weather is still extremely cold. Because what determines the cold and heat of the weather is not just sunlight.

The locals in Shanghai have a folk saying of "Starting the Nine" (起九), indicating the process of the weather gradually becoming warm and harmonious. Counting from the Winter Solstice, nine days later is the first nine, eighteen days later is the second nine, until ninety-nine eighty-one days. It is recorded below, and I think that there are many foreigners in Shanghai, and they also want to read it, but according to the author's six or seven years of experience, the increase in heat is a little later than in the proverb.

"From the first nine to the second nine, greet (i.e. salute) without taking out your hands. On the third nine, the twenty-seventh day, the fence is blown to pieces. On the fourth nine, the thirty-sixth day, sleeping at night is like sleeping in the open air. On the fifth nine, the forty-fifth day, the sun opens the door. On the sixth nine, the fifty-fourth day, the tree tops are green and vibrant. On the seventh nine, the sixty-third day, the cloth quilt is spread out at both ends. On the eighth nine, the seventy-second day, cotton clothes are exchanged for lined clothes. On the ninth nine, the eighty-first day, clothes can be taken off casually."

Children's Weekly

Prelude to Christmas

— Tianzhu

Christmas is coming soon, and the children are happily waiting for its arrival; this holiday is traditionally the sweetest day for children. Santa Claus, with his white hair, amiably sends a large number of gifts, everyone eats candy, plays with toys, and enthusiastically holds a grand celebration. On this day, children are filled with excitement and joy.

But children! For more than two years, the flames of the War of Resistance have spread throughout every corner of the motherland. Our Christmas has also been spent in the deep waters and scorching heat of the motherland. Although many children in the isolated island are sheltered at home, they still eat well and dress well, and everything is very comfortable. They are truly the darlings of paradise. However, let us look at the little beggars wandering in the streets and the refugee children in the shelters. What kind of life are they living! Is it because they are gluttonous and lazy? No, no, it is all caused by the ruthless artillery fire of the invaders.

The northwest wind is blowing very hard, and the weather has turned into severe winter. Children on the isolated island are living two different lives, one is comfortable and enjoyable, and the other is hungry and cold.

Children! Christmas brings joy, but today, when we are planning to celebrate Christmas, do not forget the suffering group. We should have the spirit of "sharing weal and woe," mobilize the children in the city, and launch the "Christmas Saving Disaster Relief" campaign, eat less candy, buy fewer toys, and use the money saved to help the children in distress. The amount may not be considerable, but by accumulating little by little, and by gathering sand into a tower, there will be good results! All the strength is accumulated from bit by bit.

Children! Let's respond to the "Christmas Saving Disaster Relief" campaign!

A Story of a Czech National Hero

— Xufeng

Since the Czech Republic was annexed by Germany in March this year, the entire Czech Republic has been under the control of the German National Socialist Party's terror. At the same time, heroic resistance has also been constantly manifested.

Now, the entire Czech nation is devoutly saying the name of Al Palmer. He is a national hero. But he is not a great person, he is just a locomotive driver.

One day, he drove a train from Brno to Rhineland. The locomotive was towing fifty freight cars, each guarded by a German officer from the Special Service Department, because it contained eight hundred machine guns and eight hundred world-famous Biron cannons (which are the best in the world) from Brno to Germany.

The train advanced north along the Moravian fountain. Al Palmer cheerfully sucked on his short pipe, smiling slightly at the German soldier who was watching him from the side, while pointing out the famous scenery to him.

At this time, he gave a signal to the fireman next to him, and the fireman raised his shovel and hit the German soldier's head. The German soldier's head was cracked open and he fell down heavily.

Al Palmer pulled the brakes and shouted to the fireman: "Jump out!" The fireman quickly jumped out of the car, fell down and got up, and hid in the deep forest. Then Al Palmer pulled off the governor and drove forward at full speed. When he reached a turning point, there was a sudden deafening explosion, and the things loaded on the train turned into countless fragments, flying in the sky. It turned out that a large amount of explosives had been buried in advance by Al Palmer and his comrades.

In this way, eight hundred machine guns and eight hundred Biron cannons were seized from the hands of the cruel enemy. Al Palmer was placed in a coffin by his comrades. His face wore a smile, like a victorious hero.

Sacrifices—Ming-er's Record of Fleeing from Disaster, No. 47—

— Bai Zheng

In that village, one can find ancestral halls of all sizes everywhere—dilapidated, brand new; desolate, tidy; narrow, magnificent. From the various styles of these ancestral halls, one can draw a conclusion: if the descendants of a surname are wealthy, then their ancestral hall must be brand new, tidy, and magnificent. Otherwise, it must be dilapidated. However, although the ancestral halls are of various styles, they all have the same great admiration for their own surname's ancestors. Therefore, the sacrifices held in the spring and autumn seasons every year are considered a very important ritual by the villagers.

This was a day of bright spring sunshine, and also the day for holding the spring sacrifice. The women of the village all wore bright red paper flowers in their hair buns (this is a special custom in the village; on the first and fifteenth of each month, and on festive occasions and sacrifices, women except widows must wear flowers). That morning, they were already very busy, slaughtering livestock, cooking sacrificial dishes, washing sacrificial vessels... because each family prepared sacrificial dishes to sacrifice to their own family's ancestors.

The ancestral hall, which had been closed for a long time, opened its doors. Many people were sweeping, wiping, moving tables and chairs, hanging paintings and scrolls. By noon, most of the ancestral hall was ready. The long tables quietly awaited the sacrificial dishes brought by each family. A high and large stone table, a pair of stone candlesticks, and two rarely seen large candles stood tall on the candlesticks. At this time, the villagers participating in the sacrifice came one after another, carrying dishes, carrying baskets... a scene of chaos. Ming-er, who liked to meddle in everything, of course, somehow got busy and walked towards the ancestral hall. This is not surprising, because he had never seen it before, how could he give up this great opportunity? He stepped into the door of the ancestral hall without hesitation. At that time, someone carried two large and white pigs and followed him in, placing them on specially made wooden frames, decorated quite luxuriously. More and more people gathered to watch the ceremony, shattering the cold and quiet atmosphere of the ancestral hall, and the noisy sounds filled the entire hall. The men in the village all wore long robes, mandarin jackets, and top hats, coming one after another to participate in this grand ceremony. However, women did not have the qualification to participate, and could only watch the ceremony from the sidelines. This is an excellent example of the Chinese emphasis on men over women. When an elderly person walked in, the hall became a little quieter. After a burst of trumpet sounds, the sacrificial ceremony officially began. The elderly person (Ming-er later learned that he was the clan elder) recited some words that Ming-er did not understand. Then, eight children (of course, male) took plates and stood in two rows, walked to the sacrificial table in the center of the hall, placed the things on the plates into the empty plates on the table, and then retreated. Then, both the young and the old offered things in the same way. This took about a quarter of an hour. With the master of ceremonies shouting "Kowtow," all the men in the hall knelt down, performing the three kneelings and nine kowtows with great reverence. The women watching the ceremony did not even have the qualification to kowtow, indicating that they were not descendants of this clan. Ming-er felt very unfair in his heart, aren't women human? And those women really underestimated themselves, engraving in their minds this unreasonable custom from ancient times, "Women are lowly," which was very deep and not easy to break. Some of those women were laughing as they watched, not knowing the lowliness of their own status, but Ming-er felt very sorry for them.

The sacrifice ended with Ming-er's resentment, and the sound of trumpets playing in the hall and the sound of firecrackers exploding outside the door seemed to be celebrating the victory of male power!

New Year's Card

— Zhang Xin

Everyone knows that the New Year is coming soon. When I think of the various joys of the New Year in the past, I can't help but smile.

I received a New Year's card in the morning, which reminded me. So I went to a nearby bookstore to choose and buy some. Although there were some for three or four cents each, they were not very elegant, and the usable ones would eventually cost several dimes. Being frugal, how could I be willing to buy them? I had to retreat. But this is a necessary social item.

The second New Year's card came. After I looked at it carefully, the problem of New Year's cards was immediately solved. It turned out that he made it himself with stationery. Moreover, everyone can make a New Year's card. The method is as follows:

Cut a piece of Western-style stationery horizontally into two pieces, then fold it in half. Then, draw a picture on one side with colored paints and gold and silver powders (mostly snow scenes as the subject matter. Gold and silver powders can be purchased from paint stores). Then, write a few artistic congratulatory words and each other's names in black ink inside the paper. This will become a generous and practical New Year's card. Moreover, the recipient can keep it as a souvenir because it is made by a novice.

In these difficult times, we should save wherever we can. Therefore, I hope children can imitate this in their spare time, so they can save money for other uses.

Little Science

— Ci Kai

Things with pointed feet like cameras need at least three feet to stand steadily. Because: "Three points determine a plane."

The floor is a horizontal plane, the wall is a vertical plane, and the slide is an inclined plane. If you remove two feet from the camera, and the tips of the feet touch the wall and the slide, it means that the two points of the foot tips can be arbitrarily joined on any plane. If there are three feet that can all "touch the ground," and you move it horizontally, if you want them all to touch the wall or the slide, one of them will always not fit. Because these three points have already determined a "horizontal" plane; once the plane is determined, it will not fall over.

The Blue Dwarf (13)

— Ai Li

Although Ah Li was not a timid girl, her heart was filled with terrifying thoughts at this moment. However, in such a dark night and in such a dark forest, not only could she not see any of her relatives, but she couldn't even see a single person. Naturally, it was easy to make her nervous. In this summer season, she thought there wouldn't be wolves, but there might be bears attacking her. At this moment, the sound of birds chirping in the distance, intermittently reaching her ears, also made her secretly startled. Suddenly, a bat flew by and happened to hit her shoulder, which scared her even more.

She groped in the dark for a long time, still not knowing which way to go. She kept bumping into tree trunks, clearly not finding a path and still lost in the depths of the forest. Ah Li walked another distance, still unable to get out of the forest, so she sat down on the ground and couldn't help but cry loudly. After crying for a while, she thought of the stories she had read before, which said that some people who were lost could find their way with a compass, but unfortunately she didn't have a compass on hand. But then she thought, in such darkness all around, even if she had a compass, she wouldn't be able to see the cardinal directions, so where could she find a path?

Just when Ah Li was in despair, she suddenly saw a little light, a tiny light, flickering through the many trees. She wondered if it was a star or a firefly? But stars don't fall from the sky, and fireflies aren't that big. It was clearly a light, and it was coming towards her step by step. She didn't know whether she was surprised or happy in her heart. She had already resigned herself to this little life, thinking that she would just starve to death or be bitten to death by a bear. She never expected to find a way out of desperation and that someone would come to save her. She looked earnestly at the location of the light, which was indeed getting closer and closer, and she could already see that it was a lamp being carried by a person; this person was short, seemingly a child. Ah Li's heart thumped involuntarily, thinking that this child, could it be her younger brother Ah Li? But then she thought, it couldn't be Ah Li. In this time before dawn, her uncle and aunt would never let Ah Li come out to look for her. But looking at the way he looked, he was clearly a child. Ah Li didn't care who it was and shouted first, "Hey, come and save me! I'm lost in the forest!"

The lamp flickered in the darkness for a while, then shone towards Ah Li, getting closer. Then, it made a surprised sound and said, "Huh, who is it?" Ah Li looked intently, suspecting that she was still dreaming. It turned out that the person, although not wearing blue clothes, was short in stature, clearly a dwarf! She looked closely at his face again and suddenly remembered. Seeing his bright eyes, she knew that this person was the dwarf old man she and Ah Li had seen earlier in the hotel window.

Entertainment World

Mussolini Loves Watching Movies

— Hua Zhi

Mussolini is also a movie fan.

Before he entered the political arena, he spent many days of the year immersed in movie theaters. After becoming prominent, he still maintained a strong interest, often wearing plain clothes and secretly leaving the Palazzo Venezia to go to movie theaters, sitting in the back row, without anyone knowing who he was. When the Prime Minister's shadow appeared on the screen, the audience stood up and cheered, and he would do the same with everyone, enjoying himself.

Italian literature and art have always been famous, but the film industry is very backward. This spring, Mussolini specially ordered his eldest son to organize a "Film Script Review Committee," offering a reward of 100,000 Italian lire to solicit excellent scripts from all over the world, with content that was anti-communist and promoted fascism, preparing to do it on a large scale. People who are qualified to apply must be from countries that signed the Anti-Comintern Pact; works from other countries will be rejected. But before the script even reached the final review, the countries of the Anti-Comintern Pact had all dispersed like birds and beasts, making peace with each other. Mussolini was inevitably quite disappointed.

Before the outbreak of this European war, Mussolini once met with Hitler. The two talked about the rise and fall of film art. Hitler mentioned that the Nazi Party's film company was putting the famous German song "Lorelei" on the screen, costing tens of millions of marks. The scenery was striving for magnificence and grandeur, and it was preparing to use "sexy" shots for the first time, etc. Mussolini fully supported it at the time and was willing to designate a piece of East African colony as the location for the film's outdoor scenes. Just as the two sides were about to start cooperating, war suddenly broke out, and they had to urgently prepare for war. Mussolini's film business was also declared to be stranded.

Joan Crawford, Star of "Woman," Talks About New Clothes

— Xin Liang

Listen to Women in Strange and Gorgeous Clothes

"Women spend a lot of money on clothing in order to dress beautifully," Hollywood's famous female star, Joan Crawford, told people. "Women probably have this idea, that the more expensive the clothes, the more fashionable and modern they must be. But in fact, that's not the case. Many times, as long as the clothes fit and suit the personality, then even those plain and simple clothes are quite pleasing to the eye. When women know that beautiful clothes don't have to cost a lot of money, how happy they should be in their hearts."

This red star continued to say to people, "Actors, because they want to stand out and make themselves look like a 'star' at all times, they are willing to spend most of their salary on making all kinds of novel clothes. Undoubtedly, their concept is wrong."

"I can say very frankly that the clothes I wear are still made three years ago. I absolutely oppose discarding clothes that can still be worn and are not very old; I also know that women's clothes change every year, but it doesn't matter, as long as you can modify them and modify them creatively, then we can definitely make full use of the existing old clothes."

Miss Crawford also solemnly said that every piece of clothing should be practical, durable, and comfortable.

"Even if you wear the most fashionable and popular clothes, but if they don't fit your figure and are not practical, then even if you wear them, you will still feel stiff, uncomfortable, and ugly."

Finally, she also told us that her clothes cost an average of $16.50 each, and her shoes cost $7.50 a pair. Of course, when there are banquets or dances to attend, her clothes are always a little more expensive.

Yang Wenying in a Guest Role in "Wen Su Chen"

— Photographed by Jiao Chao

Ideal Novel

Chaplin's Dream

— Bai Di

Winter has already arrived, and the biting cold wind pours down from the sky in gusts. The bare tree branches are swayed by the wind, making a mournful sigh.

Chaplin returned home from the film studio, the day's work leaving him exhausted. Although he had already gone to bed, the excitement in his heart prevented him from calming down. Because the culmination of his months of hard work—"The Dictator"—would soon be completed. He felt that this was sacred work, and millions of movie fans around the world were eager for the early release of this film.

He went to bed, took a small amount of sleeping pills, and then fell soundly asleep.

Suddenly, a voice rang out in his dream. It was a rude roar. The voice said:

——Stop your work! Foolish man! Many people in the world are not satisfied with your work. They all hate you, like they hate a warrior! And they will immediately destroy your work, even destroy your life!

But another voice began, a weak cry, filled with misery and misfortune.

——Dear Sir, continue your work! Most of the oppressed people in the world support your work. Moreover, they see a glimmer of dawn in your work. Sir, we will use all our strength to be your strong backing! Complete your work, and all the righteous people in the world will thank you!

A third voice rang out. This was a voice full of justice, determination, and courage. It said:

——That's right! Most of the oppressed people in the world will support you. Don't listen to the evil curses of those demons! Take courage, gather all your courage, and persist in your work for justice! Because this is the path that points to light and freedom

The clock on the wall struck three times, and Chaplin sat up straight from his dream and said to the enlarged photograph hanging on the wall,

"Yes, I will bravely persevere."

Mysterious Girl Tan Ying Left for Hong Kong the Day Before Yesterday

— Xiong Jian

Xinhua is cooperating with Hong Kong's Nan Yue Company to promote the South China market and make films in Hong Kong, distributing both Mandarin and Cantonese copies. In the past, works such as "Tears of Rouge" and "The Weaver Girl Descending to Earth" were products of this cooperation. Recently, Xinhua officials plan to film the story of the Green Screen Mountain from the Water Margin: "Shi Xiu and Pan Qiaoyun," and decided to take advantage of Wang Yin's presence in Hong Kong filming "Peerless Beauty" to have Wang Qian direct the film. All the main characters have also been assigned, with Wang Yin playing Shi Xiu and the role of Pan Qiaoyun played by the "Mysterious Girl" Tan Ying. Tan Ying has not acted for a long time, but this role is quite suitable for her personality, and it is predicted that she will receive good reviews. After Wang Yin went to Hong Kong, he once returned to Shanghai to collect materials for the play. Now, Tan Ying has already set sail for Hong Kong on the French President Doumer ship the day before yesterday (the 14th). Once she arrives in Hong Kong and the script is written, filming will begin.

Weekly Quiz

— Published by Xue Weihan

Game Seven: Drawing Fire from Under the Cauldron, Red Moves First to Draw

Chess News: After the Six Kings Tournament, Hong Kong held another Three Kings Tournament. The participants included the Seven Provinces Chess King Zhou Deyu, the Four Provinces Champion Dong Wenyuan, and the Macau master Zhou Zhen. During the match between Dong and Zhong, Mr. Zhong lost two games in a row and gave up. In the match between Zhou and Dong, Dong won six games. He voluntarily stopped the competition after winning one game, and Mr. Dong won the championship. Mr. Dong is now setting up a chess challenge at the Sincere Company in Hong Kong for fifteen days.
